<Author>EastCost3
<Content>Great Stay with Family My wife, son (12 years old) and I stayed at the Millenium Hilton a few days before New Year's Eve. The purpose of the trip was to catch some shows, shop and see the sights. We purposely chose to stay away from midtown and the Times Square areas. The Millenium was at a great location to get away from the crowds and experience Lower Manhatten, but still convenient to Broadway, Central Park and shopping. There were several subway stations very close to the hotel.The hotel met and exceeded our expectations for a NYC hotel. We had a junior suite on the 51st floor that was super clean, comfortable and fairly spacious. Our room had views of the rivers, Statue of Liberty, Ellis Island and into the Trade Center's work site. My son really enjoyed the bird's eye view and watching the construction on the WTC site. The construction activities did not bother us.The hotel's front desk, bell and security staff were very friendly, helpful and courteous. The front desk was able to accommodate our requests for early check in and late check out. Although parking was expensive ($65 a day/SUV), it was on site and the parking attendants were very efficient during a very busy time.It you are looking for grand public spaces, a lot of restaurants and an ostentatious atmosphere, this is not your hotel. But, if you are looking for an upscale hotel in a great location with modern, very comfortable and clean rooms with great staff, then you may want to consider this hotel.

<Author>Tyjen
<Content>Definitely NOT a 4 star.... There are some positives about this hotel... The location is great (out of the way but well connected to the subway/mass transit), the rooms are a good size, and the view is incredible. However, we experienced a number of problems which made the stay almost unsatisfactory.First of all, we came in and wanted to check out the refrigerator... but it wouldn't open for some reason. Then we noticed there was a cup missing and hair and a stain on the bed. We immediately called Guest Services and they advised they would send an engineer and house keeping up immediately to rectify the issues. We then went out of the room for a few hours to go explore. When we came back the bed was in exactly the same condition as we left it and the refrigerator still would not open. We called back down and they replied, Oh, house keeping said they already changed the sheets. This was, however, was a complete lie because we had moved pillows and the sheets around and they were untouched. After explaining this to the front desk manager she replied, Oh, OK. Do you still want the sheets made up then? Flabbergasted, I replied, Yes! That's why I called the first time 3 hours ago!! I also made sure to tell them to come after 6:30PM b/c we were in a rush to get to a dinner reservation (it was 6:00PM when I called). Five minutes later, however, both housekeeping and engineering came up and I had to explain again to please come back at 6:30. Fortunately, this time when we returned from dinner, all problems were solved... or so we thought.The next morning when we took a shower, there were long and nasty hairs all in the tub and on the tile wall of the shower. We hadn't noticed it the day before because we hadn't used the shower. This clearly showed us that they either did not clean at all or did a totally unsatisfactory job of cleaning. Overall, it's a decent hotel - fortunately, we paid a lesser rate through Priceline. However, I'm a gold member and have come to expect a certain level of service which, had I paid full rate, I would be completely dissatisfied by this stay. Management was, in general, indifferent and lackadaisical Only stay here if you get the cheapest rate possible. .

<Author>cocolinu
<Content>Great hotel!!!! Loved it!!! Clean, comfy,spacious,relatively close to dining, shopping, etc.; yet not so close to Times Square, Central Park, etc. Otherwise, no hidden fees, no over-billing, no problems. The noise from the construction at Ground Zero was not insupportable either, they did offer earplugs and told us that we could request what they called a sleep machine were we to have trouble sleeping. As one can imagine, after an entire day of sightseeing,who needs earplugs?  We were really fascinated by their extremely fast elevators: they go from the lobby level to the 43th floor,where our room was located, in the blink of an eye. The way they just fly between floors is awesome! The only minor complaint we have was the fact that in the room adjacent to ours, a.k.a that shared an in- room door, there was someone who really enjoyed watching loud TV past 12 am...situation that of course,created some tension between us, as one of us felt like calling the front desk and informing them of the situation. Otherwise, we wouldn't doubt staying at this hotel again. On a personal note, we were really sad to see the Towers gone...which of course won't last long as they are very busy rebuilding them.

<Author>moe-moz
<Content>couldn't have been better Just returned from a spur-of-the-moment honeymoon in NYC. We booked our room by naming our own price through priceline, and - to our great fortune - ended up at the Millenium Hilton for 6 nights at a very reasonable rate. Our request for a quiet room was accommodated, and I can honestly say that I don't remember sleeping as well for so many nights in a row. The bed was comfortable, the sheets were soft, the room was immaculate, and our view of the bridges and Brooklyn was fabulous. The staff was extremely helpful - my husband received great advice on romantic things to do in the city from the concierge and upon hearing that we had just gotten married the desk staff sent up complimentary chocolate dipped strawberries and sparkling wine. We weren't staying on the side that faced the WTC construction, but during the daytime the noise was not that bad on the street level. Also, the hotel is perfectly situated next to several subway stops and Century 21. Our stay couldn't have been better.

<Author>BritainDC
<Content>Reasonable rates, great rooms, fine location With reasonable rates, excellent spacious rooms with great views of the city and a decent location close to a busy subway line this hotel quickly became my preferred place to stay in Manhattan.It may not have the immediate proximity to major New York landmarks as a hotel near Times Square, but the Millennium Hilton is less than a block to the E line. I've always found it easy to get around town using the hotel as the starting location. The nightlife round the hotel is non-existent, so you should budget for a $20 cab ride back at night -- or just take a subway back for $2.The rooms are very large and the furnishings, as with any Hilton, are excellent. Huge, comfy king beds that you can disappear into, a few chairs and tables arranged around the room, and well-sized bathrooms that are always clean.One of the biggest draws for me is the swimming pool at the hotel, which is a real treat. It's never too crowded and it's a pleasant way to unwind. There's also a sauna -- though the heat is only slightly above room temperature, so I guess it's more of a lukewarm paneled room -- fitness center and a decent business center that I've used a few times.The staff are friendly and the concierges I've dealt with all have encyclopedic knowledge of the city. They add to what is always a pleasant experience staying at this hotel.

<Author>BlueCupcake
<Content>Fantastic View!! The view was absolutely amazing from the 49th floor corner King Suite. The computers were down when we checked in which seems to be a problem quite a bit...could be all the construction next door at the World Trade Center though. The rooms were meticulously clean and the housekeepers know their jobs and are very efficient. You never see them, but your room is always clean and ready. The location is great - lots of nice, casual restaurants around. Got a great manicure/pedicure around the corner and sushi. Walked up to Canal Street for shopping. The lobby is horrible with all the tourists coming in and using the bathroom. It could not possibly be any smaller and it is quite astonishing how poorly laid out it is. The front desk is helpful though and just ignore the bellman and take your own bags. It isn't worth it to hail one down when the elevators are so close and quick. The beds are really soft, but the pillows are too soft so had to ask for some foam ones. They came up pronto! The only problem was our family coming to visit - they were staying at another hotel and they would ring our room often and the phone never rang. Important as they were going to leave on a flight back to the UK that night so they were in the lobby for an hour waiting for us. We didn't even know they were early. Overall, worth every penny. Use the AAA rate!

<Author>Elithecat
<Content>I love this hotel I go to one of the online sites where you bid on hotel rooms when I travel to NYC. I'm always *so* happy when my bids land me at the Millenium Hilton. I really can't believe it --I used to live in NY so feel odd staying in hotels there, and I consider myself more of a boutique hotel person than someone who frequents a big chain. But I'll say in all honesty the the bright, professional, competent and considerate Millenium staff treat you like it's a boutique hotel. Each time I've come in on the red eye from the west coast, the staff has suggested that I go freshen up in the spa and then store my luggage until my room is ready. That a.m. shower alone sets this place apart from others which (simply, reasonably) expect you to wait until check-in time. But I have also had splendid luck with my rooms at the Millenium --I'm always on a high floor, and the views over the Hudson or the Brooklyn Bridge are magic. The hotel is also very close to nearly every subway line you would want to travel on, and it's walking distance to great restaurants and sweet parks. The WTC construction is ongoing, but noise has not been a problem when I've stayed at the hotel. Just in case, each room I've been in has carried a letter from the general manager explaining the construction plan. The letter comes with a set of earplugs (so far, I've used them on the plane and in other hotels!)

<Author>MoToBride
<Content>Construction noise not bad Paid $180 per night plus taxes on Priceline.Hotel was as expected from other reviews. Pretty much all the rooms face Ground Zero and the construction which was kinda interesting to watch. Room was VERY spacious for any hotel standard forget NYC standards. My #906 was the lowest floor with rooms on it (I asked for this as I heard the wait for elevators was long on the upper floors and I wanted to be lower in case of an emergency). The construction did not bother me, the sound was little more than regular city noise you get anywhere. I did wake up once or twice around 6am cause I think they were moving some big piece of metal around or something, but fell right back asleep. I slept in til around 1030 one day  didnt use the earplugs or need to ask for the noise-reduction machine offered on checkin. There was some noise that came through from the corridor if there were people talking but that was rare as my impression was the hotel was far from full.Had breakfast in the restaurant once, $$ but quite yummy (blueberry pancakes). They were pretty easy about doing substitutions if you wanted. There was also a buffet for $23.95 but it was quite small and no pancakes!Bathroom was great, shampoos etc. were replaced daily. My only annoyance was somehow my phone would only ring in the bathroom, the cordless in the bedroom was connected to some other line which I could use to call out but no incoming calls. Free 800 calls were appreciated. You have to pay for internet use, not sure how much as I had my blackberry.Employee service was excellent, fast checkin. I had some packages delivered and one of the security people worked very hard to locate them as they were initially missing. I also had a bit of a problem locking my door (my fault) and a security person was there within seconds. Someone also came right away to look at the phone issue, although they were not able to fix it and I didnt have time to bother calling again.Accessibility was excellent with the E train being right outside and virtually all other subway lines within blocks. I also walked to the Brooklyn Bridge. Century 21 is right next door too. Cab from Laguardia cost about $30-40 depending on the route  direction as this hotel is further downtown that the midtown hotels.I would recommend Woodbury Common Premium Outlets (you can drive there, about 1h, or take the bus from Port Authority $40 rtn which I did), much better deals than in Manhattan despite July 4 weekend sales.I did not use the pool or any other amenities so cannot comment.

<Author>JMRN
<Content>Very nice downtown hotel! We usually stay at the Courtyard Times Square South when coming to NYC. We opted to stay the night of July 4th at the Millenium Hilton in order to have closer proximity to the fireworks and the South Street Seaport. We had a king room which was about what we expected; not huge but certainly big enough to move around and room for our bags. The room was very clean; had a huge flat-screen tv, a large bathroom with Crabtree  Evelyn toiletries, and a great view of the waterfront/Ground Zero. We were on the 45th floor and still had a little street noise, but that's to be expected in NYC. The construction didn't start until late in the day; possibly because it was a weekend, but again, the noise didn't really bother us. There were earplugs provided in the room for those who are light sleepers; or I suppose you could request a room on the opposite side of the hotel. We didn't take advantage of the pool or restaurants, so I can't comment on those. The bed was comfortable, the shower was great, and I can't think of any reason not to recommend this hotel to anyone.

<Author>BCBrewster
<Content>Nice NY Option Walking into a hotel room and seeing earplugs offered by the management, with an apology letter is not usually a good start, but this is New York and any room near the street has some noise issues. The 24-hour cacaphony is part of NYC. Asking for the highest room available is wise if you have problems with noise.The rooms all seem to overlook Ground Zero, which is undergoing massive construction, but the contruction is presently at street level. Thus, a birds eye view of Ground Zero and a good view of the East River. The rooms are brand spanking new (newly renovated). They are large for NYC. The beds are wonderful. There is Internet access (I guess for a fee, since I use WAN). I found staff helpful and efficient.Various subway routes are within very easy walking distance. The terminus of the E train is here, but others pass through. Because this is Wall Street area, there is not a lot going on at night. Best options seem to be to walk east along the south side of Ground Zero and across the pedestrian overpass. Along the river, there are various options. The better bet in the evening is to take the subway north to Union Square, Times Square, etc., where there are more options. In the morning, you will see the Wall Street workers streaming from the subway like lemmings, all headed the same way.The gym appeared decent, with various machines. I did not eat in the building.Overall, this hotel is ideal for a businessperson who will be doing business in the Wall Street area. Though it is out of the way for most tourism, the subway makes everything proximal in NYC.This area is a bit far from airports. You could take the A train from Kennedy and be very close by. From LaGuardia, you would ideally take the E train, but you have to get to the train stop by taxi ($15) or bus. From Newark, you would need to go to Penn Station, then a subway south.

<Author>willw
<Content>noisy elevators i was given a room on the 47th floor looking out over the East River and Brooklyn Bridge. on the first night there was a fantastic firework display to celebrate 125 years of the brooklyn bridge and i got an awesome view from my room. the room was large, great flat screen tv, and kept perfectly clean by the twice daily housekeeping. an ice bucket, bottled water and chocolates was provided daily although i didnt touch the mini-bar because there were warnings everywhere saying it would start to charge you automatically for things if you moved them, whether or not you actually consumed anything. beware! bell staff and front desk staff were very pleasant and efficient. my only problem was my room backed on to one of the elevators (they are high-power and high-speed for reaching the upper floors quickly) and the elevator machinery was quite noisy. but luckily i'm a sound sleeper. the location of the hotel was great, easy to find (at the bottom of the E line of the subway) and easy to get around to other places, battery park for the statue of liberty and ellis island is just a few blocks away, and a short walk in the subway interchange takes you to chambers street for the direct subway (A line) to the AirTrain and kennedy airport. i would recommend this hotel to anyone except if you are on a tight budget, but it was still better value than some other hotels in the city.

<Author>skhMontreal_Quebec
<Content>terrific hotel, convenient location My mother and I just came back from a 4 night stay at the Hilton and thought it was a beautiful hotel. We had a very spacious room with 2 double beds on the 37th floor facing the city, not the construction. No problems with construction noise at all. The only down side to this area is the amount of construction going on, but the hotel is located right across the street from the subway (or right down the street depending upon your entrance or exit). The dept store Century 21 is located next door, we walked to Battery Park to take a view of the Statue of Liberty and passed other shops on the way. You would think for the price charged, a free breakfast would be included, but I gather that's not the norm in expensive New York. The hotel booked the hop on/hop off bus tour for us, where the pickup was a block away from the hotel. Soho/China Town/Greenwich/Times Square was a mere 10-15 min subway ride or if you kept walking up Broadway, you would eventually walk right into these districts. Very close to Tribeca restaurants. It takes about 2 days to orient yourself on how the subway runs and where the streets are located, but all in all, we were very pleased with this hotel where we were able to use accumulated points (otherwise, no way could we have afforded this).

<Author>TravelinGatorFans
<Content>Could be better, could be worse We stayed at the Millenium Hilton this past weekend for the first time. We don't spend much time downtown, but picked the hotel because it was close to an event we were attending. Overall, our stay was pleasant, although it could have been better in some areas.The construction going on at the WTC site makes getting to the hotel a little bit of a challenge, but the signs they've put up are fairly clear. We dropped off the car in the garage, where the garage attendant stood by watching as we unpacked our bags ourselves, without offering to help. Granted, the garage isn't owned or run by the hotel, but for a hotel of this caliper, it was surprising that they didn't have bell staff there to assist visitors. Check in was a snap, and a quick one at that. The woman who helped us was very pleasant, as was the one who answered questions we had later in the afternoon. Our room, on the 41st floor overlooking the WTC site, was very nice. Although we'd been warned about possible construction noise, from that height we didn't have any at all. The room was extremely quiet during our whole stay. My only complaint about the room was that the A/C didn't work well at all. It wasn't hot out by any means, but even with the thermostat set at 65 (the lowest it would go) we were all way too warm all night long. Had we stayed longer we would have asked to have our room changed.The pool was lovely, and the public areas of the hotel were very well maintained. Aside from the A/C issues in our room, the only other area where the hotel was disappointing was in the area of the staff. Granted, we usually stay at the Sofitel in midtown, where the staff are incredibly professional and courteous. But when you're spending almost $400 for a hotel room, you expect exemplary service, and the Millenium Hilton was definitely a let-down in that area. With the exception of the front desk staff, the employees we ran into were OK at best. Not outright rude, but definitely lacking the polish and professionalism I'd expect at a hotel like this. So as I said, overall our experience here was OK. I don't know that I'd stay here again, though, mostly because for what the room cost, I don't think the service was quite up to par.  
<Date>May 5, 2008

<Author>servicecomesfirst
<Content>Pretty good the second time I stayed at this hotel on the weekend of April 18-20. This was my second visit. My previous stay was in March 2008 when I paid $169, and I was a bit shocked that the rate was double this time -- but I guess this is not out-of-line for other similar hotels in Manhattan. Last time the construction noise wasn't a problem ( I was on a high floor), but this time they put me on a lower floor (26) and I could hear the droning all night long. I found the staff to be pleasant and helpful. For example, I was looking for a newspaper at 7 AM Saturday morning: the gift shop hadn't opened yet, so the bellman went on a crusade and brought me back a paper. One small criticism of the restaurant: I am very picky when it comes to my morning coffee and the coffee there isn't very good -- it tastes like it is made in one of those huge steel containers you see in cafeterias. As others have noted, there should be free wireless internet in the rooms given the high room charge. I like the location of the hotel, as the financial district is quiet on the weekends and I enjoyed going for a jog at nearby Battery Park. All in all, I would recommend the Millenium.

<Author>gweneddk
<Content>Very nice hotel; difficult location for tourists The room was great--very clean, larger than I expected, with luxurious bed linens and a comfy king bed. Main problem was with the heating/AC unit--it ran constantly and was very loud. The hum of the A/C drowned out any construction sounds from Ground Zero, but we could still hear water running through the pipes from adjacent rooms. They really should have put some better soundproofing in.Staff were polite and helpful. They held our bags on the last day for no charge. We didn't eat at the restaurant, but the room service and mini bar prices were quite honestly outrageous. I could go down to the entrance and get a hot dog and can of soda for $4, or get a can of soda from the minibar for $6! There is not a whole lot of food near the hotel, so we tended to eat in midtown before heading back to the hotel.The next time we come to NYC we will stay closer to midtown. It became a pain to have to take the subway everywhere especially since they were working on some of the lines we needed over the weekend so we had to change lines a few times. But for a business traveler I think the hotel fits the bill.

<Author>wolvespremier
<Content>Fantastic experience - see New York at its best ! I went to New York for a trip in December 2005 and had a great time at the Millenium Hilton. We stopped on the 39th floor and had a breathtaking view of Ground Zero. The hotel was the closest hotel to the Twin Towers and the staff are always keen to tell you stories. There is even a rescued flag framed in the reception area from the building that was salvaged on the terrible attacks in September 2001. Make sure that you ask for a front facing room as the views are simply stunning. The views from the rear will encompass Brooklyn Bridge. We didnt get chance to use the swimming pool facility but did enjoy the breakfast everyday which had the most delicious muffins I have tasted . . . ever! and you can eat as many as you want :) Nearby there is a underground station which is accessible to most places with ease, the hotel is situated just a short walk to the harbour front where you can see the Statue of Liberty. There are several restaurants nearby but dont make the mistake of ordering a starter as you wont eat the main . . . food was fab, but there was just too much of it - even for a strapping 6ft 5 lad like me. The staff in the hotel were all very friendly and nothing was too much trouble, when I ordered Champagne to the room it was there within minutes and there was never any fuss. If you are a shopaholic be sure to check out the Department Store next to the hotel 'Century 21' I think the name was - loads of bargains to be grabbed, fantastic prices and lots of choice. The hotel was also a short walk from Wall Street as it is situated in the heart of the financial district so there tends to be an after-work crowd in the hotel bar at night and that is where you can really soak up the atmosphere and mingle with the locals. Overall a thoroughly enjoyable trip - lovely hotel - the only thing I wouldnt recommend is spending New Years Eve in Times Square, although its nice to say you have done it you cant see much and you need to start queuing at 3 - 4pm in the afternoon in the freezing cold . . and if you need the toilet, well you lose your place! Still I cant complain, an unforgettable experience which has left me with fantastic memories . . enjoy!  
<Date>Mar 22, 2008

<Author>giulietta429
<Content>average corporate hotel, lost of construction, good room service I stayed at this hotel for two days. It was convenient to the business meetings I was attending. The check-in took a while -- the clerk (only one, despite a long line of people waiting to check in) was nice.The hallway was covered in plastic (the hotel is undergoing construction) and looked very industrial/non-plush. Not impressive at all. I got a king room on the 43rd floor (4306) with a view of the WTC site, the river, and the city beyond. The room was small, but the furnishings were modern. I liked the bed linens and great pillows (I think I used all 6!), and a flat screen TV was a nice touch also. I also liked that there was a coffee maker with two cups. I always like to have a hot beverage and don't necessarily want to order room service every time I need a cup of tea.There was an alarm clock (not too hi-tech), and the obligatory mini-bar with a selection of very expensive drinks. One of the drawers was taken up by snacks (I tried the pretzels -- 1oz bag for $4.50! - but that's to be expected, and they were fresh).The bathroom, also small, had a weird toilet with very low water level and low flow of water in general. The shower head and the fixtures were not too modern.The toiletries by Crabtree  Evelyn were pleasant smelling. The cleaning person refilled all of them (unfortunately, no cotton balls or Qtips) the next dayI wish there was a bathrobe and slippers! The safe was useful, though.The gym was adequate -- much nicer than I've seen in some other hotels, with several cardio machines, weights, water, towels and magazines. I also wanted to try the heated pool that looked relaxing, but it was rather crowded with families/children and I decided to pass. The business center was inadequate, in my view -- you could not even acces the internet for free. What kind of business hotel is this?I thought that room service (I had 2 dinners and 1 breakfast) was good -- the food came when it should have and was fresh and tasty, but the menu choices were fairly limited, especially if you don't eat meat/want something healthy.I would recommend the shrimp wrap (I had it twice!) and the heathy breakfast (eggwhite frittata was beautifl -- large, hot, full of veggies, and just delicious; juice, hot drink, and fruit cup).Finally, it was odd not to have the option of checking out via the TV, like most other hotels (even of much lower 'grade') have. I got a paper bill under the door overnight (the old fashioned way) and had to call the front desk to check out.Overall, this was okay, but I won't be disappointed if I never stay here again.  
<Date>Mar 15, 2008

<Content>Great Staff, Location, Rooms, Loved it! My teenage son and I flew in for a short business trip  to see the parade. To start off, the doormen begin your stay with a warm greeting. <Author>NatBriKen
<Content>Best of Downtown Stayed at the Millenium Hilton for only one night, February 2. Booked directly through Hilton by phone. Easy 7-10 minute taxi ride from Penn Station, or there is a subway stop next to the hotel. This hotel is directly across the street from the Path Station and Ground Zero. Also, across the side street from St. Paul's Church (built in 1766. This church was where George Washington went to pray after his inauguration. It is also the church who's amazing stained glass windows didn't even crack as the towers-across the street-collpased. It was a relief/aide station during the months following the attacks. There is also an old cemetary in front dating back to the Revolutionary War). Trinity Church, South Street Seaport  Museum, Battery Park, Tribecca, City Hall, Chinatown, etc. are also nearby. My 8 year old daughter and I had a Corner King on the 37th floor. I have to say, from check in to check out, we were both treated with great respect and courtousy. We were offered ear plugs or a sound machine if the noise from ground zero became too loud. We didn't need either of these things; however, there was a pounding noise from the site which ended at midnight and began again at 6 am. (just in time for us to see the awsome sun rise over the statue of liberty!)The view from our room was amazing. The windows are almost floor to ceiling. Out one window we could see the Brooklyn Bridge and Dumbo. Out the other window we could see Ellis Island and the Statue of Liberty. We watched the ferries go by and the circle line, as well as some cruise ships on their way back home.The beds were very comfortable. The room had a large flat screen plasma TV, alarm clock radio, two phones (one in the bathroom), a Lavazza Coffee Maker with tea set up as well, and internet access (for a fee). There is not fan in the bathroom but it was very nice and the name brand toiletries were top qualitiy. The ceiling in this room was large by current standards. Don't open the minibar unless you want something...it is on sensors and if you touch it the computer thinks you bought it. One wonderful thing that this hotel has that many others in Manhattan don't, is a pool. It is located on the 5th floor next to the fitness room and the spa (where you can opt for a massage after walking around downtown all day!)The decor of the restaurant and bar area were modern but not large. Windows overlook ground zero on one side and St. Paul's Church on the other. My daughter liked watching the cars and people go by outside below us while we ate dinner. She was waving at people who actually waved back at her. That made her day. Be advised that they do have a children's menu but they do not offer substitutions. Also, if you don't want your burger rare, say so! The menu had a lot to choose from. Something for almost all tastes.I would definately stay here again if I needed to be downtown. The reception was wonderful, room beautiful, pool fun and food good. There is also a starbucks downstairs and a real hot dog vendor around the corner. There is a lot to do downtown so take advantage of this wonderful area of Manhattan. Check it out and stay at the Millenium Hilton!  
<Date>Feb 18, 2008

<Author>nififer
<Content>The views are simply out of this world!! The standards in this hotel are simply superb. We had a corner mini suite on the 50th floor looking out on to the Hudson River and with the Statue of Liberty and Ellis Island in plain view as well.The room was immaculately clean, with tea  coffee making facilities and two huge TV's. However noise will become more and more of an issue as the rebuilding work continues. This hotel has a super location downtown - you are next door to Century 21 only a few minutes walk to Battery Park (and the Liberty/Ellis Island ferries) a few minutes to South Street Seaport and the subway is right at the hotel door for midtown and uptown trains.My only criticism - and I stress only, is the concierge arranging transfers back to the airport - ours was a yellow cab with no meter running so the journey back to the airport cost far more than the journey from the airport. Insist on a metered taxi at all times.A wonderful stay and a hotel I would definately return to.

<Author>MEBr
<Content>Great property but be aware of the noise You can count on the Millenium Hilton quality at this Financial District property - great amenities, cleanliness, friendly and helpful staff. We were lodged in a junior suite on the 28th floor with wonderful views of the city facing west, including the Hudson River, and to the north, looking uptown. We also got a great room rate, but beware that the hotel sits right next to the giganic construction project going on right now at Ground Zero and they are working just about 7X24. The hotel will supply you with ear plugs (didn't really help me) and the option to obtain a white noise machine (with a $200 deposit refundable when you return the machine). At some times during the night, construction noise can get quite loud. The room was wonderful - good space with large windows, great bedding and very comfortable mattress. The bathroom was spacious, with a large vanity granite counter. Housekeeping was always available to make the pull-out sofa bed, even at 1:00 am. The hotel bar on the 3rd floor is so-so in the way of what an average hotel bar would look like. I would love to give this hotel a big thumbs up, but would do so with reservation since the contruction noise was very audible and at times irritating in the middle of the night.

<Author>LemanandAngieHarris
<Content>Outstanding Hotel in Lower Manhattan - Top Marks!! We booked to stay at the Millenium Hilton on Church Street in Lower Manhattan NYC for a 3 night long weekend (7th to 10th December 2007) to celebrate my 40th birthday. The hotel is out of the hustle and bustle of the main attractions such as Times Square so the traffic  pedestrian noise levels are non-existent from the hotel rooms. We were welcomed by very polite and cheerful hotel staff and found our room to have an incredible view over Ground Zero on Floor 53 (of 54) ... we could also see the Statue of Liberty from our room - east facing rooms look over the East River towards the Brooklyn, Manhattan and Williamsburg Bridges. Construction of the Freedom Tower which is to stand in the place of the former Twin Towers is to be ready in 2010. Although friends who had visited several weeks before us had told us that construction noise could only be heard from 8am to 9pm we found this to be different on our visit. Extended hours are being worked in order that the Freedom Tower is finished on time. We could hear construction noise (even on the 53rd floor) from 5:30am to 11:30pm. A letter of apology from the hotel management was on our room desk the following day and to be honest the noise was not really a problem so do not be put off - just be aware of it if you are travelling here.We bought the hop on hop off bus pass (All Loops Tour) but only used it once as the subway and the taxis were very cheap and easy to use. Also the top of an open-top bus in December is VERY cold so you don't want to spend too much time up there! The subway station starts and ends directly opposite the hotel. The fare is $2 per person per trip and this will get you to 42nd Street (A, C and E Trains) and a block away from Times Square and all it's entertainment  shopping in less than 15 minutes. Don't take with you any preconceived ideas about the subway - it is cheap, clean, roomy, quick and VERY safe. We will use this method of transport around New York on every future trip now. The hotel concierge are superb so make sure you use them and their vast knowledge of the area. We were advised on transport, restaurants, bars, shopping and local sites. If you stay at the Hilton Millenium you MUST go into St Paul's Chapel next door where memorials and tributes are made to those brave people who lost their lives and loved ones in the 9/11 attacks. It is a very humbling, moving and peaceful place - we were very touched by this experience and were priveleged to have spent time here.There is a GREAT deli around the corner on Vesey Street. Breakfast and lunch are delicious and very cheap. Try the hot pastrami with mustard  pickle on rye - simply delicious. Please look at the photographs on the walls in the deli too - again some very moving pictures taken from 9/11 in the deli sheltering fire and police crews - very thought provoking. You can also find a superb French restaurant on the east side of the hotel - from memory I think it was on John Street but I can't remember the restaurant name - you'll know it when you see it. We had a bottle of wine and butcher's cut steaks which were divine all for $80 - quality!In summary the Hilton Millenium is outstanding. Rooms are very comfortable, clean and have all the requirements expected from visitors including entertainment system (huge Plasma TV / Playstation / WiFi / Tea  Coffee / Ice / Mini-Bar, etc.). Room service was superb  delicious as well as very reasonably priced for a hotel. I have read many reviews on this site and find it a little fickle that people mark this hotel down because they see Ground Zero as a construction site or that they were kept awake by people arguing in the hallway - this is no contribution to the rating of this hotel. We rate the hotel as very highly recommended. We would definitely stay here again without hesitation and hope that our review helps you make your decison as to where to stay in this wonderful city! Enjoy!!!

<Content>Great hotel, not the most interesting area Very nice hotel, but they are a little unlucky with the noise at the moment. The WTC reconstruction is behind schedule and the constucters are being fined for every day they fall behind on certain deadlines. This is not the hotels fault though. That said I would wait a few months before going to stay there as the work is almost 24*7 right now.The room was great, as was the bar, room service, reataurant...everything you want from the hotel. Of particular note, the ear poppingly fast lifts. I found the staff to be very friendly and sympathetic about the noise and as our room was not ready on arrival they treated us to free drinks at the bar (which more than makes up for it).I didn't like the area the hotel is in too much. I was aware it was a business area but I guess since 9/11 a lot of other businesses closed as a result and even on a weeknight, there are fewer options than elsewhere so you may need to travel..thankfully most of the metro routes seem to cross around here so its a good location if you are planning to use the train system a lot.Overall I was very satisfied. I'd probably try another area next time but would recommend this hotel to others.

<Author>Kelly&Tony
<Content>Nice hotel but do not stay here whilst WTC construction is still in process I searched many a website to find the perfect hotel for our 5 night stay in New York and I eventually settled on the Millenium Hilton. The photos on the website looked very nice and the value for money was good given our 5 night stay included New Years Eve. I had no doubts really that the hotel would be fine given the Hilton name.The hotel itself is very nice, clean and with stylish decor and first impressions are very good.Ours problems however started at check in. I had pre-booked a king room with a city view only to be told there were none currently available, so we had 2 choices, wait for a room to become available later in the afternoon (it was 4pm when we tried to check in) or take a lower room. We decided to wait for our room with a view that we wanted.We were pretty tired after the very long journey but sat patiently in the hotel bar for our room. After an hour we went back to the desk and were allocated our room on the 48th floor. The room was very nice with a view right over what was the WTC and the Statue of Liberty in the distance. I was perfectly aware that there was construction works going on prior to booking the hotel but presumed the works would stop in the evening and continue in the morning and as I am someone who sleeps well I did not think it would pose a problem 鈥?how wrong could I be? I decided to have a quick kip before heading out for something to eat on the 1st evening, I laid on the bed for 2 hours between 5 and 7 and didn鈥檛 sleep a wink due to the very loud construction noises. On our way out for something to eat we asked at reception what time the works would stop, we were told maybe 11pm sometimes earlier sometimes later (not very helpful) we asked for some ear plugs which they appeared to have plenty of.The long and short of it is that the construction went on ALL night and we did not sleep a wink, even with the ear plugs and a pillow on my head. We phoned down to reception in the morning and asked to be moved to a quieter room or alternatively to relocate us to another hotel and we had no intention of staying where we were and having 5 sleepless nights.We took our luggage down to reception and went out for the day. We were told we would be allocated another room. We returned to the hotel at 8pm to find we had not yet been allocated a room, after about 陆 an hour they found us a new room. It had twin beds and no city view but the room was quiet and we were too tired to argue the difference and the receptionists did not seem too bothered anyway. I intend to take this further with Hilton now we have returned home.On the positive side as before the actual hotel is very nice. Ideally located for down town Manhattan with subways on the doorstep costing $2 for a single journey anywhere in Manhattan. New York is a fantastic place, everything you think it will be and a place you have to visit at least once. The shopping is amazing and very cheap in comparison to the UK, there are many bargains to be had. The food is also fantastic, we ate in Fish in Greenwich Village and had whole lobster for 拢15.New York at this time of year was very very busy, I would definitely return again although probably at a quieter time of year. If you go when its busy expect to queue for everything.With regards to the hotel I would definitely not stay here again until after the construction has finished and would not recommend to anyone to stay there at the moment.

<Content>Great Location, shame about the noise and elevators! I stayed for 4 nights at end of Dec 07. The location of the hotel was great - I much preferred being here to Midtown. I had a view of the water and Statue of Liberty, plus the construction site at WTC. <Content>Christmas at the Hilton Last year - Oct 2006 my family and I stayed at the Hilton Millenium, the visit was really good, I would have given it a 9/10. But our second visit December 21st - 27th 2007; sorry Hilton, but you have let your sides down. I would give you a 3/10 on this visit. I thought a year in advance and with a request like that - easy to plan. My children were with me (21,19,16) and I wanted them to see the breathtaking skylines over Christmas. We did have a king sized junior suite, nice size, shower worked, maid service good, bed made, clean towels and room kept tidy. One thing that really got me.. I must be honest here too, the bar staff in particular (main bar and resturant bar 3rd floor) were not friendly (anyone with an ice pic?) - more so on the rude side. I have travelled with Hilton for business throughout Europe, service was better, staff approachable and friendly. But overall... Would I go back? No. I like to feel a bit more of a welcome. I suggest Hilton management to get the bar staff on a customer relationship course. And teach them how to serve with a smile.....

<Author>sparky6798
<Content>excellent stay We just returned from our first trip to NYC and stayed the last 3 days at the Millenium Hilton, and we overly pleased with the stay. We had stayed in Times Square for the first 2 nights of our stay and were a little worried about leaving that area for another hotel.But we were more than pleased with our choice. The hotel is a Hilton, and that speaks for itself. Very modern , clean and staff very more than willing to help on any occasion.We booked a room through Hotwire for $244/night and felt that was a great price for that hotel in NYC at that time of the year.We had a deluxe room with a king bed ( as promised) and had no complaints whatsoever about the room. It did overlook ground zero, and it was a bit noisy on some mornings but we were on the 21st floor and what we heard at that level was nothing to complain about. Yes there was some noise, but nothing that you may even notice.We didn't eat at the restaurant but we heard that it was very good.They have a great pool, and fitness center. The business center had all the amenities , but charged for use of the internet, (perhaps in my opinion the only negative thing about the hotel). FOr such a hotel for this price, I think internet access should be available at no extra charge.Staff were great and answered all of our many questions about NYC and tried to help in whatever way they could.The location of the hotel is in the downtown area, which was not a concern for us, as the subway was very convenient and got us to where we needed to be in 10 minutes.Overall a fabulous time in NYC and at this hotel. Would definately recommend this hotel, and we would stay there again

<Content>nothing less than superb! We stayed here for my 40th birthday and it was nothing less than superb!I was our second trip to NYC. Worth every penny!Victor, the extremely efficient guy who took our reservation ensured we got one of the few (14) smoking rooms of all of which are on the 54th floor and ours had a excellent view over Jersey with an eerie eagle eyed perspective over the WTC site. The location in Downtown NY is close to Wall street, right next door to Century 21 and two mins walk from Abecrombie  Fitch which made shopping so easy and cab fairs up town are cheap.Check in was instant! The door men are first class, everyone of them friendly and funny but the numerous concergie's vary. One guy, Joe, was condescending and rude and managed to mess up our dinner reservation for my big four oh but another guy who's name slips my mind gave us excellent advice on where to catch the Arsenal V Chelsea match - Nevada Smiths on 3rd ave between 11th  12th which had an absolutley brillaint atmoshpere - packed with chanting fans of both persuasions, half of them expats and amazingly, many avid new york soccer fans! We ate breafast and dinner in the hotel both of which were excellent with super service. The bar staff are great, especially the retired cop guy who didnt fail to set us up a freebie after several rounds and tips. They talk freely about the horendous events of 9/11 when incredibly the hotel survived any serious structural damge despite being directly opposite the WTC. (on our first nitght we watched the movie WTC in our room and it was weird to be looking down on the site at the same time - God bless America!)Nonetheless the Millenium closed for two years following those disasterous events and required substantial superficial rennovations which contribute to its pritine appearance today. The public areas are excellent, the rooms/bathrooms superb. The leisure cetnre is small but adequate with a nice pool which is a rarity in Manhattan but sadly there was no jacuzzi!The view from the upper floors are stunnning! On our final morning we awoke with a start to find a guy cleaning the windows which momentarily scared the cr*p out of us as it is the last thing you'd expect to see at that height! Check out was completely hassle free, the bill had been settled automaticaly and a reciept posted under our door on the moring of departure and the hotel stored our bags untill we left for the airport at 4pm. We had to nip into Century 21 to buy an extra suitcase to transport our purchases!All in all, this is an absolutley superb hotel at the price!Cant wait to go back!MP1

<Author>illtryanythingonce
<Content>A great choice if the price is right! We stayed at the Millenium over the long Thanksgiving weekend (arriving after the parade!) while visiting our daughter who lives in Brooklyn. Having previously stayed at hotels in Times Square, we opted for something different this time around. I saw a really good nightly rate online and called the hotel directly and got the same rate. I asked for a City View King room and was thrilled when I walked in to a very large room, extremely clean, the bed was so comfortable with lavish linens (lots of pillows!). We were on the 51st floor, looking directly west (over the WTC site) and out over New Jersey. We could see south to the Statue of Liberty and north up Broadway. The window in the 51st floor elevator lobby afforded a terrific view of the Brooklyn Bridge (and Brooklyn) and the river. The plasma TV on the wall was terrific, very modern desk and dresser. Comfortable chair, large closet - lots of well-placed lamps and reading lights. The bathroom was very clean with lots of counter space (hair dryer, really really nice towels and lots of them, the usual shampoo, etc.). A nice touch was that an umbrella was in the closet for our use (didn't need it) and a safe was provided as well. The lobby was nice (a bit noisy with all the comings and goings) with a lobby bar but when the bar was full, there were no other places to hang out. The concierge was great, very good recommendations. Bellmen were johnny on the spot and apologized for the delay as we were leaving that there were no cabs to be had (we were leaving during Monday rush hour) but did call one specifically for us to get us to the airport on time. We really enjoyed our stay at the Millenium and will again (if the price is right). We were slightly amused that for the price we paid we didn't get free internet (neither in the room or in the business center) while the Burger King down the street (as well as other businesses) did! Even our cheap hotel room in Eau Claire, Wisconsin offers free WiFi!! Also, while the plasma screen TV was really nice and big, the restricted number of cable channels was a disappointment. Couldn't they offer a few more movie channels (only had HBO) or the more popular cable channels? Not that we watched too much TV, but after walking all day it was nice to unwind in the lovely room. Don't hesitate to stay at the Millenium if the price is right for your budget (we paid about $300 inc. taxes per night which we thought was a bargain in NYC).

<Author>Dubskin
<Content>very good choice I and my partner stayed at the Hilton for four nights for a long weekend in New York. The hotel is in the downtown area but easily accessible with public transport and a taxi ride to midtown is about $ 17. We arrived after a transatlantic flight in the evening and were immediately whisked in with the luggage all taken care of. The receptionist (Angie I think her name was) was extremely helpful as our request were a smoking room and a high floor. She excelled at this and we were given a fantastic room on the 54th floor overlooking ground zero and the Brooklyn Bridge. The room was exceptionally large by New York standards and had all the amnesties you could wish for: good internet connection (for a very reasonable $12/day), LCD TV, mini bar, large bathroom and excellent bed. The service overall was very efficient and friendly. The concierge helped us making restaurant reservations and taxis were flagged down very quickly.The only downside of the stay was the varying service in the bar next to the lobby. The prices for the very same drink orders seem to vary between staff and at one point the bar tender refused to allow us to take the drinks upstairs (his explanation was that they were short of that particular style of glasses, well then order some more).There are limited choices in the area for good food, but we tried Les Halles on 15 John St which was a good basic choice, 2 minutes from the hotel. Other than that you may have to travel a bit to get high quality restaurants. We loved Lever House Restaurant on 390Park Avenue.I can highly recommend the Millenium Hilton (even if the spelling annoys me) and considering the normally ridiculous room rates in New York the Hilton is definitely a bargain.

<Author>dave1013
<Content>Met my expectations Wife and I were at the Millenium for three nights on a Diamond award stay right before Thanksgiving 2007. Location of this hotel was perfect, as we eschewed the car and took Amtrak up from Washinigton, DC. We came up out of the PATH station at the World Trade Center station, and the hotel was staring us right in the face!Upon checking in, the front desk clerk told us our room was not ready. I asked for an upgrade and we were promptly assigned a corner junior executive suite on floor 38. That room was fantastic, with an impressive vista of the WTC site. We knew it was going to be noisy thanks to previous postings here but as with many others, it didn't overly bother us.Subway stations are within two blocks of the hotel, taking you just about anywhere you want to go in the city. At the end of our stay we saved probably $30 by taking the subway up to Penn Station to catch our train to Pennsylvania, instead of hailing a cab.During this trip, I fulfilled a lifelong dream of visiting Ellis Island. Battery Park, where you catch the ferry, is a 15-minute walk. We had dinner at the South Street Seaport one evening, another pleasant 15-minute walk.Only possible down side of the entire visit is that things pretty much fold up in the evening, but there are ways to compensate for that. Overall we had a fantastic time and I would stay here again. I want to thank all the previous posters for their insightful reviews and helpful suggestions.

<Author>teachers_on_tour
<Content>Great hotel This is a really nice hotel. It provides everything you would expect from a hotel in this class, and it is a great deal at the weekend when the financial district is quiet. Excellent beds, helpful staff - no problems at all. Century 21, a truly wonderful department store - discount but not tacky - is right next door. However - it is not in Midtown or anywhere near it if you like to walk. We did not find the subway as convenient as it might have been: some stations are closed because of Ground Zero rebuilding and on the long weekend we were there, ticket machines wouldn't take any notes, only coins. Having just arrived, we didn't have many coins - so take some! Buses don't take notes either. You could buy a pass with a credit card, but obviously you need to be travelling a fair bit to make it worth it. None of this is the Millenium's fault - but be aware and come prepared. One other problem with the location is that there are very few restaurants within walking distance. It's a very nice hotel, but be prepared to use public transport a lot. Previously we had stayed in Midtown and were certainly spoilt for choice with restaurants close by, but of course, you pay more. For the money - we paid about $400 Australian per night - it's great.  
<Date>Nov 21, 2007

<Author>rachelw77
<Content>Good value, good location NYC is getting more expensive by the month and it's really difficult to find a decently priced business-type hotel in Manhattan these days.....so I was pleased when I found the Millennium Hilton. I booked directly via hilton.com and paid 200 US dollars, a great price for this location.The rooms are spacious, modern, with fast internet service and are exactly what you would expect from a Hilton hotel. The hotel is definitely designed for business travellers....there is very little lobby space, few extra amenities and not much of a concierge service. Wall St is just a short walk away, and the hotel is on top of a subway station so it's easy to get around. Bargain hunters will be pleased to know that Century 21 is right next door too.Yes people may moan about the view, but what do they expect?! Look beyond the ground zero construction site and there is a perfectly nice view of the river, all the way across to the statue of liberty....

<Author>susanderek
<Content>All round winner We stayed here for 5 nights - 10th through 14th October. The hotel is in a great location for exploring the downtown area, and a very short walk to subways on a number of different lines. We walked along to the South Street Seaport on two mornings for a relaxing coffee on the deck as the boats passed along the East River.The rooms were a mixed bag. We had a double for the first night which turned out to be two queen beds 鈥?certainly not enough room for three to sleep comfortably. The beds themselves were incredibly comfortable 鈥?just not big enough. Luckily we had booked a Junior Suite for the next four. What a difference. On the 29th floor, it was very spacious, and had three huge plate windows looking down towards the Battery, and out to the construction site that is Ground Zero, with the bustling traffic on the Hudson a lovely way to greet each morning. I didn't find it off-putting at all 鈥?it's just a hive of activity and a symbol of a people determined to recover. The iconic 'cross' section of the original building stands in front of the church just a little way up Church Street, and that is still moving.We loved our big 42鈥?plasma screen, but it didn't improve the quality of the programmes! That's not what we went for of course. The rooms had internet access for $12.95 per 24 hours. Yes it is noisy 鈥?they work from early morning to late (and I mean late) at night, except for Saturday night. So I bought earplugs, which worked a treat. $4.99 and you have hundreds of Duane Reades to choose from!We ate in a few places nearby. Go to the Stage Door Deli across the way for great breakfasts and real theatre courtesy of the staff. Have you ever seen a bagel fly? Well, you can here. We also ate in the Woolworth Building Kitchen which was excellent value. The hotel's restaurant serves up similar fare but is more expensive and less atmospheric than either of these.Being right next door to Century 21 is another plus 鈥?even if only for getting in early morning or late evening before it gets far too busy.Staff were courteous and helpful, and ensured that our pick-up to the airport was on time.I'd go back tomorrow. In fact I wish I could...

<Author>rachime
<Content>Met expectations The Millenium Hilton met our expectations. Fab price for the location and amenities- walking distance to Battery Park/ Statue of Liberty departures, multiple subway stops nearby. Most of the areas around the hotel have walkways for pedestrians now, so we didn't have any trouble getting around. Be aware of construction noise, but it didn't keep me from having a good night's sleep in the super-comfy bed. We had a view from the 27th floor overlooking the WTC site, but we found it more interesting than sad- good to see progress. Refrigerator and snack drawer are on the weighted system, so don't plan on storing food or beverages of your own. This hotel IS in New York City- parking is limited and expensive if you have to use it, and there are only two single bathrooms off the lobby. (A woman behind me in line was very rude with complaints about this fact.)

<Author>tpbel
<Content>Thank Goodness for the Hilton !! When I was planning the trip to NYC as my daughter's 18th birthday present, I asked her if we should get a good hotel, or not bother, as we wouldn't be doing anything other than sleep in it. Well, thank goodness as any precocious 17 year old would, she wanted to spend the extra for a good hotel. So I chose the Millenium Hilton from the City  Show website, and actually got a pretty good deal.As it turned out, my daughter was EXTREMELY ill for the trip, for all of the 5 days we spent there. It started when she fainted on the plane out there (a BIG BIG thank you to the wonderful guys on Continental Airlines who helped her out with oxygen). So we got to Newark, got our taxi to the hotel, and my daughter didn't leave after that (except for an hour in Bloomingdales and a pre-booked helicopter trip). She couldn't walk one block so didn't even see Ground Zero.So we were stuck in our fantastic hotel room on the 44th floor, with our excellent view up towards the Empire State. As a busy working mum, I actually found the enforced stay very relaxing - we caught up on all of our movies on the big flat screen! The staff was very helpful, and the beds extremely comfortable. This hotel made what could have been an utterly miserable trip, bearable.I had a meal in the restaurant one evening which was very pleasant. Also, the hotel is right next to Century 21, which is ideal for cut-price shopping. And the World Financial Centre is also worth a look, as well as the church across the road which at that time still held the memorabilia for the lost loved ones of the 9/11 tragedy.The only problem (and why I'm not giving it a 5 rating) is that there were no instructions by the phone on how to ring an international call back home to Ireland, and I inadvertently dialled various numbers (including to Africa apparently!) and I had to work hard with the reception staff not to be charged an exorbitant amount.I think I'd like somewhere more central next time, but if you want to be downtown, this is the place. My daughter recovered when we got back home of course, and we know someday we'll be able to laugh about it (just not yet!).

<Content>Loved It We stayed at the Millenium Hilton Sept 14 to Sept 17. We got an excellent price of $249.00 per night on the Hotel website. We arrived at 8:00 am on the 14th and were given a room despite the fact that check in is at 3:00 pm. The hotel lobby although not impressive was clean and functional. The bed was great. The room was well appointed and had a flat secreen television. All of the staff we dealt with were friendly and helpful. I would definitely stay here again. As for the negatives, there is loud construction at the WTC site and this hotel is right across the street from Ground Zero. We did not really have a problem with these things though. We did not try the restaurant or bar at this hotel. This hotel is definity worthy of a four star rating unlike many four star hotels is NYC. <Author>HRich
<Content>Romantic New Year City Break My now-husband but then-boyfriend and I visited New York for the first time at New Year and chose this hotel due to it's down-town Manhattan location and star rating.Upon arrival, reception was very busy, and we were a little dissapointed by the staff, who were perfectly professional and efficient, but as a result - not overly friendly. That aside, the service was excellent, if not with a smile.The room was a comfortable size, with full length ceiling to floor windows on one side, a wide screen tv with cable and plenty of storage as well as a lovely bathroom.We had a room on the 29th floor (I think) which had spectacular views overlooking the ground zero site. One of the first things we did was go and visit the site, an emotional experience, having wached those awful events live on the news all day when they unfolded.We were only in the city for a few days, over the New Year period, and found the hotel an excellent home from home after travelling around the city seeing the sights. Century 21 is right next door and full of great bargains, and as soon as you get used to the subway system, the city is very easy to navigate from here. We walked to Wall Street, and over to the Statton Island ferry port (were you get the ferry to go to the Statue of Liberty) as well. This was not a 5 minute walk, more like 20 - 30, but enjoyable, even in December.New Year's eve was a greatly anticipated event for us, and we chose to do it the traditional NY way and go to Time Sq. We had received advice to get there very early, and we thought 6pm would be early enough. Boy we were wrong. We finally made it into a pen about 10 blocks back from Time Sq, where we were unable to get out for food, drink or toilet breaks. We stood for 6 hours with little idea of what was happening in the centre, and by the time the ball dropped, we were ready to drop ourselves!The party atmosphere was a little jaded by this point, but we still cheered, hugged the poeple we'd met in the crowd, and then my husband proposed. This made it all a lot more bearable, of course! If I was to recommend a NY New Year to anyone, I would say they should book into a hotel off Time Sq, or book at a restaurant nearby, as this will make for a much more pleasant experience! If not, you probably need to arrive at about mid day to get a spot in the centre, which I'm sure would be worthwhile.All was made more wonderful when we returned to the hotel, hungry and cold to find that NY truly is the city that never sleeps. Through room service we were able to order a pizza from the parlour down the road. It was delivered to our room at about 1 am and must have been the best pizza I have ever eaten!All other meals we bought outside of the hotel, so I'm afraid this was our only experience of room service, which I must say was excellent.  
<Date>Aug 31, 2007

<Author>Jeff_stack
<Content>Fantastic hotel in excellent location When: Thurs Aug 9 鈥?Mon Aug 13Price: Priceline $150/nt ($178/nt after taxes). Rack rate $202+taxThe Hotel:Fully renovated after 2001. The hotel was very new looking, very clean and the staff were excellent. Bed and pillows were the most comfortable I have ever slept on. Each room has a 42鈥?plasma TV but I did not see any HD tv channels so you can鈥檛 really take advantage of it. There is a small bar fridge but you can鈥檛 use it because it is full of their items and if you move anything the electronic sensors will bill you. There was a ice container we would fill up to keep our leftover cheesecake good until the next day.Elevators were crazy fast, we were on the 50th floor and never had to wait longer than 20 seconds for an elevator and the full trip was under 30 seconds. Pool and fitness room were quite reasonable. Check in time is 3pm but we there is quite a rush at that time. We arrived at 11am and simply dropped off our luggage and pre-reserved a room (ask for one on the side away from Church St. for lovely views on the Brooklyn st bridge and to avoid the near 24 hr construction at the WTC site. Parking is super expensive at the hotel so we just dropped off our luggage and parked at a parking lot under the FDR drive by the Brooklyn Bridge (take Frankfort St toward South St) and you can鈥檛 miss it. $21/day taxes included for parking in a fully insured and monitored car lot.Location/Activities:The hotel is on Church street in SOHO Financial district right across from the big hole in the ground that was the world trade center. Metro entrances 2 min walk from the hotel but another 5-6 min underground to get to the line. ~15-20 min by metro to Times Square and other great areas. 10 min walk to the Staten Island ferry which is a faster and cheaper (free) to take a boat past the statue of Liberty. The financial district is much quieter at night than midtown but my wife and I never felt unsafe walking the streets to the hotel at midnight after a broadway show. There are cheap ways to eat in the area. Our favorite nearby was a 24hr buffet ($5.74/lb of food) at about Fulton St and William St. Also a nice bistro and grocery store at about Liberty St and William St. We brought our own cereal and bowls and simply bought a liter of milk from the pharmacy on Fulton just east of Broadway each morning on our way to the TKTS booth for a super cheap breakfast. The TKTS booth is at the corner of John St and Front St about 10 min walk from the hotel. This TKTS booth opens at 11am for that evenings and the next days matinees shows. Be aware that the tickets are pretty much all $60 for Broadway shows (they only really discount the most expensive seats) and they tend not to have the most popular shows (Hairspray, Rent, Legally Blond, Mary Poppins, ect.). Also note there are really no Broadway shows on Sunday nights. We did however see Chorus line, Curtains, Phantom of the Opera and The Drowsy Chaperone. The TKTS booth in Times square sells that days matinees and evening shows and tends to have a better selection but longer lines. It also opens later (2pm) so it wrecks your day more. Food before broadway shows can be had cheaply on Eighth ave between 44th 鈥?45 th st (Subway, burger and pizza joints, ect) but I highly recommend 鈥淛uniors鈥?on 45th St just west of Broadway. $10 sandwiches and burgers and the best cheesecake in the world ($6.50) 鈥?I recommend the devils foodcake or the chocolate mousse cheesecake. They have a takeout counter but if you want to sit down show up early.Over all:Excellent hotel. Worth the 4 stars and in a great location for those who don鈥檛 mind being a little further from the hustle and bustle of Midtown.

<Author>WebBrown
<Content>Good stay at Millenium Hilton I stayed at this hotel with my wife and 17 month old daughter from July 20-22. The hotel rooms have clearly been renovated recently and they've added some nice touches. The bed was very comfortable and the large flat screen t.v is built into the wall. The bathroom was nicely renovated and decorated as well. We had a room on the 20th floor over looking the World Trade Center site. Although, it is not the most pleasant of memories, I the view was a good reminder of all that happened that day. I booked the hotel through priceline and got a great rate and a great room. I even requested to be moved initially because the original room they gave me was too close to the elevators. I was moved without a problem. The front desk staff were courteous and helpful. The location of the hotel is perfect is you're looking to be in the SOHO/Financial district and close to the Hudson River. It's only about a 10 minute walk to the river. I highly recommend this hotel.

<Author>goodwig
<Content>Excellent But Be Cautious! I have stayed here a number of time, only because Priceline.comhas given me the opportunity at a low rate.The hotel is sleek, modern, and high rise; as a result of beingrebuilt after 9/11. It is directly across the street from the construction site for the rebuilding of the 9/11 complex.Thus, it can be noisy and the main entrance, Church Street, isoften closed.Consequently, the price is low because of these inconveniences,but you can reap the benefits of a beautiful hotel by requestinga high floor facing the Brooklyn Bridge and the east side oflower Manhattan. I have stayed in many hotels in NYC and thiswould be my first choice if view is important.I have stayed on the 9/11 side of the hotel at a high floor andgenerally you can avoid the noise while enjoying a truly marvelous view of the Hudson River, New Jersey, 9/11 site, and the Statue of Liberty.If you want to stay in lower Manhattan, stay here. You can walk toSouth Street seaport, Wall Street, Battery Park, City Hall, theBrooklyn Bridge, etc.Just remember to be smart and request a room on a high floor.Staff are accommodating and the amenities are first class.Once the new World Trade Center site has been completed, the prices at this hotel will skyrocket !

<Content>Lovely Hotel! Although I am late in writing this review, I thought I had to get something on here as I thoroughly enjoyed my stay at this hotel.. <Author>Kazakie
<Content>A pretty nice hotel Generally when visiting NYC we use points to stay at the Waldorf-Astria, but since they've changed to seasonal rewards and the Millenium Hilton had really reasonable weekend rates we thought we'd give it a whirl. We were upgraded to a corner suite (Diamond status), were issued breakfast coupons on checkin (the breakfast here is 10x better than the Waldorf's) and there are several subway lines there that makes it very easy to go through the city - and oh yea, there aren't 101 tourist walking all around like times square (but the tourist aren't too bad by the Waldorf either). The hotel is much nicer than I thought and pretty up-to-date including large flat-panel TV's (but I hope you didn't come to NYC to watch the tele) - I think it was fully refurbished after Sept 11. The elevators to the high-floors are super-fast. This is a compounding effect. Because the elevators are so fast you get to your room quicker, which means it can make more runs therefore less people per elevator ride, which means less stops on your way to your room, which means you get to your room even quicker. We're independent travelers, so don't use services from the hotel staff much, but we experiences some wonderfully positive and knowledgeable people, and some staff that we're so keen either of those qualities. The only other would be that there is no free wireless in the lobby and no wireless (paid or otherwise) in the room - they do have a LAN line. ...next time we stay in NYC, we might just stay here again...

At night, I would still see people around. Furthermore, this place is not so far from China Town and Little Italy and at night, there are lots of people in the area to eat etc. I actually liked this location lots as I have an affinity for Asian food. In addition, Century 21, an outlet shop is right next door. Hotel:Initially, I requested room with a king sized bed. They honored my request. When I got up to the room, it was a bit small. I came down and asked for an upgrade. They told me that there was no upgrade available. They gave me a corner room with a queen sized bed instead, which was way more spacious. Ask for a corner room, if you can. I did not find too many negatives to write about. The one thing that sort of irked me a bit was the hot water; it took about a minute to have hot water in the shower. The bathroom amenities were what one would expect at a hotel of this category. Toiletries were of Crabtree and Evelyn. Plenty of towels in the bathroom. There were no slippers or bathrobes, something I never really use. The bed, pillows, and sheets were all good. More importantly, there were all white. No motel styled/ flower sheets. There was a nice and big flat screen with cable channels. There was no Wifi in the room. High speed internet can be had for $5.95 a day, which I think was not too bad. I have seen high speed internet rate at $ 15/day. However, there was free Wifi in the lobby. There were ice bucket and wine glasses in the room . There was also a mini bar, which I did not use. Everything was clean and worked well. The pool was really nice. I used it everyday during my stay. I (we) stayed there for 3 nights.Service:Checking in and checking out were a breeze. They were all very efficient and gracious. Housing keeping was efficient. There was downtown service as well. Recommendation: I definitely recommend this hotel to my friends. I would stay here again in the future. I find that for the price of $260/night (including tax) I paid for, it offered a really good value. The same hotel category in Midtown probably will cost twice as much, if not more. I booked my through Hilton website. I remember that some other previous post mentioned that it costs lots. I think I lucked out by booking early.
