<Author>Grootato
<Content>Great Hotel! This was my first visit to New York city to attend a wedding and I spent weeks researching online and agonizing where to stay as I read all sorts of horror stories about bad hotel experiences in NY City. Because I noted that the Millenium Hilton got consistently high ratings from most guests I decided to take the advice of the TripAdvisor Members and book my Memorial Weekend stay there even though it's location was quite far from where the rehearsal dinner and wedding were to take place. I am glad that I did!! The hotel and rooms are as gorgeous as the pictures in Trip Advisor and Travelocity! The location one of the quietest spots in NY. Hardly any traffic noise could be heard from my room. I don't know if it being Memorial Day weekend had anything to do with the low noise as there were workmen at the ground zero site and plenty of people in the streets but at any rate, the low noise level worked out fine for me.The hotel decor was modern and the entire facility looked very well kept. The carpeting was plush and all the brass and glass surfaces sparkled. The hotel also has its own garage for guest parking . My room was a little bit bigger in size than my home's master bedroom which I understand from some of the reviews I've read here is big by NY standards. It boasted a very large (Queen I think) and extremely comfortable bed with lots and lots of fluffy pillows and a long sausage pillow which is perfect for folks that like to wrap themselves around a pillow for support. The room and carpet were clean. There was also a large flat screenss stereo tv that was equipped with both a wireless keyboard (for internet surfing) and game controls for playing video games. The tv system would also allow the viewing and purchase of movies but I don't know the prices because I did not choose to use any of those features but I'm sure that you could run up quite a bill. There was a well stocked mini bar with beer, soda and snacks but because they're notoriously expensive I didn't dare consume any of them. There was also a dresser with two empty drawers for storing your stuff. There were two telephones. One in the bathroom and a cordless two line model next to the bed. There were two separate reading lamps on each side of the bed and a very simple to use alarm/clock radio with your choice of sounds to wake up to. There was also a writing desk that was equipped with two jacks for internet access for laptop computers. One jack was for a regular phone line modem and the second one was for DSL access. Next to the desk was a table that held an ice bucket, a wine bottle opener and glasses and an coffeemaker with cups and coffee supplies. There were also two comfy chairs, an ottoman a small table and new issues of two NY entertainment guide magazines. Next to the bed inside the night stand's drawer was a free paperback copy of Conrad HIlton's autobiography which I'm still reading. The room had it's own climate control for the a/c heat system and it worked flawlessly at keeping the room at the temperature that I set it to. There are no keys for the doors of the suites, instead you get a credit sized electronic key that unlocks the door for you. In my standard room there was also a full length mirror and plenty of lighting and seating. Two features of my room impressed me. The well appointed closet and bathroom.The well appointed closet held, a folding suitcase stand, a large umbrella with the Hilton logo and around 4 or 10 thick wooden hangers. A couple had clips for holding skirts, a couple had trouser bars and two were thickly padded ones of the type for holding evening dresses. There was also an iron and ironing board in the closet and on the top shelf your very own electronically controlled combination safe for your valuables. The bathroom was very well lit. It had a very large mirror and an illuminated magnifying makeup mirror that swiveled. There was also a hair dryer. The faux marble counter ran the entire length of the bathroom so you had lots of room for your toiletries. It also included a nicely appointed bathroom set which included facial tissue, drinking glasses and Crabtree  Evelyn toiletries (mouthwash, shampoo, hair conditioner, a shower cap, bubble bath and body lotion and bar soap) and lots and lots of fluffy towels. The shower/ tub had a swiveling shower head that you could adjust to deliver either a full stream of water or a pulsating shower massage. The water was plentiful as either ice cold or scalding hot and the water pressure was just fine. The toilet was one of the quietest flushing models I've ever heard and worked flawlessly. From my window I had a great view of ground zero and the window curtains could be adjusted to let in either a lot of light or shut it out completely. I was on the 17th floor and could hardly hear any of the traffic below. The downtown location is excellent. Hilton provided in each room a folded pocket sized map of NY city with indicators for different businesses in the immediate area as well as the locations and routes of the subway system. This little jewel of a map was my lifeline and guide during my entire stay in NYC. Meals in the hotel (like in any hotel) are expensive ($22.00 for breakfast) but there are lots of inexpensive diners in the area. Right in the next block was the Stage Door Deli (open 7 days) where I got one of the biggest and best breakfasts I've ever had (2 scrambled eggs, bacon, potatoes, toast and coffee) for only $7.00 and their sandwiches are excellent! There are also the ever present hot dog carts on almost every corner where you can get really delicious hot dogs, shishkebabs or pretzels for a very reasonable price.Next to the hotel is a large discount dept store (21st Century) so if you forgot to pack something like a shirt or tie or socks or shoes you could shop there for designer brands at discount prices. The subway was less than a 1/2 block away and easy to navigate. A one way fare is only $2.00 but you can buy a fun pass for $7.00 which gives you unlimited rides all day.However, if you choose to take a taxi to where the action is (Central Park area) I found that it will set you back around $22.00 plus tip because remember, the Millenium is waaaayyyyy downtown in the financial district. A taxi ride to the airports - I was told- can cost you as much as $55.00 plus tolls, plus tax plus tip so I chose to ride in and out of Newark Airport on the super shuttle van service which costs only $17.00 plus tax and tip. BTW you can make reservations with Super Shuttle airport van service by toll free phone or online. Their only drawback is that because the shuttle goes around picking up passengers in other hotels besides you they will require that you be ready to check out quite a few hours before your flight. For example, my flight departed at 11:00 am but their pickup time for me by the shuttle was 7:30 But, it was a reasonable trade off for the savings. And their service was really, really good. They even telephoned a reminder of my reservation to my cellphone and their cancellation policy is reasonable if your travel plans change.The Millenium Hilton hotel lobby is very nicely decorated in modern style and had a small but well appointed gift shop. They looked as good as in the pictures shown on line.The lobby also had a bar at the other end but I didn't patronize it so I can't critique it. The hotel also had a gym, a restaurant and I think that it also had a pool but I didn't check them out. Overnight shoe shine service was also available.One lobby feature that I liked was a touch screen kiosk where you could punch in your flight information and a printed boarding pass would pop out for your convenience. On the back end of the block from the hotel were a Dunkin Donuts, several small diners and a big CVS pharmacy. Around two blocks down from the hotel was a Barney's Men's clothing store (another NY institution). Chinatown and Little Italy neighborhoods were a brisk walking distance away and in those areas I encountered loud traffic and massive flocks of people spilling from the sidewalks walking cheek  jowl making me glad that I didn't pick a hotel in those areas! I wanted quiet and I got it at the Millenium.A short walk to the other side of ground zero across from the hotel and you were walking by the bay and I could see the statue of Liberty at a distance. Water taxi and sightseeing services are available in the area. I read a lot of horror stories about NY hotels trying to stick its guests with padded bills for minibar snacks that were not consumed or treating a customer poorly because they booked their room thru a discount service like travelocity but that didn't happen to me at the Millenium. When I telephoned ahead from my room to advise the front desk that I was checking out a very nice lady at the the other end told me that I had incurred no additional charges and that the prepaid travelocity bill had covered everything in my stay. All I had to do at checkout was to drop off my electronic room key at the front desk and just and walk out the door (didn't even had to sign anything) to my waiting ride never encountering any pushy doormen or bellboys. They were all very pleasant, courteous and helpful. The concierges Justin and Mark bent over backwards in giving me directions to my travel and shopping destinations and the bellhops and front desk personnel were just as attentive, pleasant and polite.There are other Hilton hotels in NY and I can't honestly say that all of them treat their guests the same way or have the same amenities but I did enjoy my stay in the big apple at the Millenium Hilton and I definitely recommend them and I would stay there again on my next visit to NYC. 5 stars!!!

<Author>caughtthetravelbug
<Content>Faultless I had a fantastic short break in New York at stayed at the Millenium Hilton, while it was quite expensive, you definately get your money's worth. I'd definately recommend it.

<Author>MartyOrt
<Content>Favorite NYC Hotel This is my favorite hotel in New York City. While it can be pricey, and it is out of the hustle and bustle of midtown Manhattan (it is on the southern tip of the island across from the WTC), if is one of the nicest properties in Manhattan. The staff is professional, and while they run the check in process like an assembly line, they get it right and get you moving quick. The rooms have always been clean when I have stayed here, the flat screen tvs are nice, but the hotel doesn't have hi def tv service so the picture isn't the best. The internet is 4.95 a night and wired only, and the room service is actually inexpensive for New York City. The pool area is clean, although the water is usually cold. There has always been plenty of hot water, and good water pressure. The Evelyn and Crabtree toiletries are nice, and there are always plenty of towels. The subway (E Train) is right across the street and two stops away from 42nd street. For someone like me its nice to go to this hotel after a day uptown with all the tourists as after 6:00 the financial district is basically deserted. I highly recommend this property.

<Author>citychicky
<Content>Beautiful Room and View I tried Priceline for the first time as we were going to the city for my birthday and wanted to stay somewhere for one night. I won a room here (4 star downtown in Priceline terms) for 200.00 per night. I used to work 2 blocks away so never really thought of staying here for a night out since it wouldnt seem like a get away necessarily but we were pleasantly surprised by our experience. The front desk was very friendly and our check in and out experience couldnt have been faster. We had a room on the 35th floor that overlooked the WTC site and the Hudson. The beds was incredibly comfortable, the tv was large and new with a good selection of channels and the bathroom was large and very clean.I do have two small negatives that I would point out. The first is that we were at the end of the hallway and there are three doors at the end of the hallway plus the staff work room so it was quite noisy with people coming and going. I could hear the noise from the hall a lot while inside the room so I ended up putting a towel under the door to try to muffle outside noise a bit.The second negative is that the mini bar refrigerator has sensors in it and so if you even move something to fit in your leftovers (as we did) they know and you will be charged for it. Luckily I saw the note that tells you this and so called to remove the charges from the bill before we left. However, if i hadnt, i would have been charged for two drinks (over 15 dollars) that we didnt take. I understand the technology makes it easy for them but future occupants should be aware of this.A note to those considering this hotel: there is very little late night activity in the area. We were going to the film festival which ended after midnight and had to cab north to find somewhere to go after the movie had ended. That said, my husband continues to rave about the hotel and called it an A+ several times during the weekend. It is a lovely and comfortable hotel.

<Author>LSelway
<Content>Great hotel, great area. I stayed at this hotel from Mar 31 - April 4th 2007. The hotel is of excellent quality. The lobby is gorgeous and the rooms are even nicer. The bathroom is roomy and comes equipped with Crabtree and Evelyn toiletries. The room I stayed in had 2 beds, as my party had 4 people. The extra bed was 25 dollars a nite, but we were not charged due to my mother being a Hilton employee (at another Hilton). The room had internet access at 5 dollars a day. I did not find that unreasonable, at all, as the internet helped us get directions for where we were going each day. We had a view of ground zero out our window on the 29th floor. The first evening we were there we ate at the hotel restaurant, Church  Dey. The food was good, but expensive. I would not eat there again, but like I said - the food was good. The area the hotel is in is a quiet one - the financial district. It was nice to return to a quiet area after a long day of crowds.

<Author>saintba
<Content>Millenium Hilton - Great rooms! Great views! Grumpy Front desk people I've been flying to New York for business every few weeks. I'm trying to hit several different hotels in different areas I need to be in. This time I had several meetings in the Financial District so I booked this hotel. I knew the view would be great but maybe a little strange since the World Trade Center is no longer in front of it. You see, this hotel is located right behind where the World Trade Center used to be. I fly from Buenos Aires so it's a LONG 10+ hour flight. Even flying in Business Class to JFK is no comfort and after a long flight I like to go right to the room. I arrived very early around 6:30 am. I encountered a very grumpy middle aged man that didn't even offer a good morning. I gave him my name and reservation number and I also showed him my Hilton HHonors Gold VIP card. I have spent a LOT of money with Hilton hotels around the world but this didn't seem to matter to this guy. He didn't even look at it.I inquired about checking in early and he said no it's impossible. He didn't say anything like I'm sorry Mr. X all the rooms are occupied. Or any other explanation. He simply said that check-in is at 2 PM and that was that. It was only 6:30 am and I was exhausted since I didn't sleep on the long flight. I was going to wait in the lounge but the chairs are not comfortable and the lounge area really isn't that nice. I checked my bag and decided to go have breakfast and do some shopping.I stayed out until about 1 PM. I was a few blocks away but usually not in this area and I didn't know it well. I called the hotel to ask for directions and said I know I'm only a few blocks away...can you help. The guy that answered the phone said that he couldn't help and transferred me to what I'm assuming is the concierge desk and no one answered the phone. I was furious. I asked a police officer and he kindly pointed me in the right direction. I get to the hotel and it's 2 PM now. I see there is still no one at the concierge desk. It's very rude when a guest is calling to get directions and you simply transfer it to an empty desk. It would have taken him all of 10 seconds to explain where the hotel was.So I get to the front desk and they give me my key. I go to get my checked bag and I had a big bag plus all the bags I had from shopping (and I did a LOT of shopping). The bellboy (or I should say middle aged man) just handed me my suitcase and didn't even offer to help me take it to my room. This is extremely unprofessional.So this was 3 things now all before I even got to my room that I was not happy about. Someone definitely needs to do a customer service seminar for these employees. This is not a way to treat a customer that frequents their many hotels around the world. I get to my room and my bad mood goes away once I see the view. They put me on the 49th floor and I have an amazing view! It's very very strange to see the big hole where the World Trade Center was. I snapped some photos that I don't know if they will allow me to post on Trip Advisor since it's not the hotel but of the view. The room size is extremely big for a New York City hotel. I guess for the u$s 350+/night range you get mostly small hotel rooms here in NYC but this was very spacous with a King size bed. The room had a 42'inch Plasma/LCD TV which was a great touch. I do the same thing in my properties that I have for rent and people really appreciate these things. The bathroom was a good size as well. Nothing luxurious but it was at least spacious.The bed was extremely comfortable with great pillows as well. I stayed a few nights and used the room service and each time they were very quick. I'd say the food was delivered in less than 30 minutes each time. The food quality was ok as well. The prices on the menu don't seem too expensive but then remember they add on like $4 service fee + 15% tip which is also fairly common these days.I'm here getting ready to check-out. I must have just gotten a grumpy check-in guy. I just called down to let them know that I didn't use anything in my mini-bar and there were at least 4 things on my bill. The nice guy that answered (said his name was Robert) was very friendly and explained that the refrigerators have motion sensors that detect if you take something out. I did move some things around to put in some water that I had but put them back in. I thought that was interesting and never heard of that before so make sure you check your bills at the check-out.I asked Robert if I could have a late check-out and he said sure, no problem. What time did you want to check-out. I told him I just needed a few extra hours. 2 PM would be fine and he said not a problem. Now that is good customer service and very friendly. He sounded younger and was much friendlier than the grumpy old guy at the check-in.All in all, I'd highly recommend this hotel. If they got rid of the grumpy ole guy at the check-in and trained their staff to be a little friendlier than I'd say it's highly recommended.Mike

<Author>Bergkamp9999
<Content>Good but some negative points Stayed for two nights on the 48th floor, overlooking the WTC site. Fantastic views and the room was a very generous size, including a small lounge area with a second TV, sofa and desk. The 42 plasma is certainly the largest screen I've seen in a hotel room but there is no inroom WiFi, just an ethernet cable connection that you pay for. You can detect over a dozen WiFi networks but you can't connect to them! The bathroom wasn't small either although the fittings looked a little dated. The bed was wide and very comfortable, with good pillows too. There's also a free safe which is always one of the main items I look for.The breakfast buffet was of a good standard but they have a la carte too. Dinner was slightly disappointing although that may have been due to my choice of dish. Costs aren't too high either.Negatives: the air-con system made a lot of noise, even when switched off. This may be a one-off and as I will probably stay here again for work, I shall update my review next time. The lack of WiFi, even if I could pay for it, was annoying, considering the typical guest is most likely a business traveller, judging by the occupants at breakfast. My final gripe is aimed at this and many other hotels; they all leave cards indicating their commitment to protecting the environment, asking you to reuse towels and save water etc. However, even if you don't leave towels in the bathtub, they still change everything every day! And it smacks of hypocrisy when they use 8 lightbulbs in the bathroom, although I did detect energy saving bulbs elsewhere in the room. The surrounding area is a bit shabby so take a taxi or the metro for your shopping and dining needs.Overall, it's a good hotel that could improve on a couple of areas but it's best suited to business travellers. Tourists are better off elsewhere.

<Author>AndreLisbon
<Content>Great Location This was my 3rd trip to NY and my 1st stay at The Millenium Hilton. I went to a congress in Westchester on March, 2 and 3 and my wife joined me after that for a whole week in the city. Wow, we had fun and the hotel was one of the reasons why we're still missing our week at The Big Apple. I had the warmest check in welcome of my life! Rooms, Housekeeping, Room Service, Front Desk, Staff in general, they're all fabulous! Liquis Assets Bar was also great for drinks before dinner. But, most of all, location seems to be the huge secret of the place. There are a few subway lines (some of them express lines) nearby which take you midtown or uptown in a few minutes (Lines 4  5 express trains). Anyway, the Financial Distric is very close to great spots like South Seaport, Soho, Lower East Side and even East and Greenwich Village. These are the places to go with their trendy restaurants and bars, nightlife and fun. But if you prefer the traditional touristic spots in Midtown and fancy the Upper East side...well, just take the 4 or 5 subway lines! There's a 4 storey shop just round the corner where you can buy almost everything to wear. Battery Park's also very close and there are some museums, bars and shops if you must stay downtown.Breakfast's very expensive though, but you can have it at so many places nearby.My wife and I will surely be back to this hotel next time we come to NY. Definately!Anna and Andre, Lisbon, Portugal

<Content>Great Hotel This is my second time at this hotel. The last time I stayed was April 2006. <Author>lolo51
<Content>Loved the Millenium We stayed at this property for four nights in February. The employees couldn't have been more helpful (with the exception of the restaurant staff). Upon arrival, the front desk was friendly, courteous and informative. My husband's a diamond member, so we were upgraded to a Junior Suite, with complementary breakfast vouchers. The room was wonderful - actually two rooms, with a plasma tv, luxurious king bed with soft, quality linens and a housekeeping staff that couldn't have been more efficient. The room had a view of Ground Zero - this didn't bother us at all. It is quite sobering but also uplifting in seeing the way New Yorkers seem to be able to handle anything they're given. My respect and admiration truly goes out to the people of this city - it is truly the greatest city on earth! The consierge couldn't have been more helpful - any question you presented him with he answered, or at least tried. Elevators were prompt - rarely had to wait at all, going up or down. Yes, the lobby is small and the lounge could be a bit larger, but if this is the only thing wrong - please. The location of this hotel is just fine - a subway station 100 feet from the entrance. The subways are quite safe and a great way to get around, but if you're subway-shy, taxi's are abundant all around this hotel. However, we found it difficult getting one - we were there when the weather was quite cold and they all seemed to be occupied! So the subway it was, with no problems at all. Being downtown, I agree with a previous review wholeheartedly - it is quiet down here and away from the craziness of Times Square - you couldn't pay me to stay there! My only complaint towards this hotel is the miserable, bored, unhappy, unpleasant wait staff in the restaurant. And the breakfast ...... if we had to pay for that food....something like $29/person for a breakfast buffet that was as cold as ice coming directly from the kitchen! The eggs were stone cold, as was the bacon, sausage, potatoes, etc. My advice - go somewhere else - anywhere else - for breakfast. Never gave lunch or dinner a chance - too many other great restaurants in this city. We are planning another trip this April and we already have reservations to return here. This is a great hotel in a great city and I highly recommend it!

<Content>Nice! Got a deal on Priceline for a Saturday evening getaway. The hotel was redone in 2003 after being damaged on 9/11. My room on the 31st floor directly overlooked the WTC site. The only drawback to the room I had (3103) was that there seemed to be some noise in the room from the elevators. It took me a while to figure out where it was coming from. Wish it was a little quieter, esp. if you're paying closer to the regular rate.But the room was very clean and nice, and I would definitely stay again if I got a decent rate!

<Content>Spacious (for downtown NY) room with a view New York is one of the few cities where I consistently book my hotels through Hotwire, or a similar service, simply because I get value for my dollar in a city where hotel prices are exorbitant. <Author>genevatraveller
<Content>Declining but still OK for NYC. I stayed at the Millenium Hilton in NYC five times between 2003 and 2006 and still appreciate this hotel even if it used to be better a couple of years ago. First I like the modern and original architecture of the hotel; then the location in the financial district and on walking distance to the seaport is convenient; the rooms are well-decorated, modern and big enough; the service at front desk is good and the concierge very helpfull. But during my last stays I noticed that the room-prices went up quite a bit and that the value-for-money is not so good anymore as it used to be. Plus their were some anoying works in the lobby and the main entrance was closed. The lobby is indeed very small for this huge hotel and seems now a bit outdated - a renovation would be welcome. Finally I was disapointed by the breakfast which used to be good but now the waiters simply don't care about you at all and I have been waiting at the bar 15 minutes before a table was ready (even if their were plenty of empty uncleaned tables) ... Millenium Hilton is still OK if you need to stay in the financial district but you should find as good or even better elsewere in NYC.

<Author>mcsimanowith
<Content>Style, Space and Hospitality My wife and I booked the Millenium for a weekend getaway before Xmas. We chose this based on good reviews and because it was one of the more reasonable accomodations given that we were smack in the middle of the holidays. We couldn't have been happier with our choice.Positives* Our room was quite spacious particularly in NYC where I have stayed in rooms which I could touch all 4 walls. * We had a beautiful view overlooking the WT Center site and across the river. * Plasma TV was great, bathroom clean, and bed quite comfortable. * The front desk staff were professional and efficient which is all I need. Get me in and get me out. * The concierge was attentive to everyone - he offered us advice on how to get to the play we were seeing, sites we were interested in and suggestions on where to eat. All were excellent. Also held our luggage on checkout day so we could do some extra sight seeing.Negatives* There was a bit of riff raff that hung around outside the hotel selling junk but it's a city so what do you expect - we never felt threatened. * Parking is outragous. We spent 85 bucks for under 2 days not including tip. * The hotel is about as far downtown as you can go without being in NJ which for some might be a drawback. However, the train and Path are right outside the hotel and fairly easy to navigate - ask someone if you need help. The first time an attendant walked us through the whole ticket process, told us where to go etc. from then on we had no problem. (The train isn't as nice or easy to use as Wash DC Metro but it was fine. I recommend an all day pass its like 7 bucks and after 2 rides you basically make your money)All in all this was a fantastic trip and I would not hesitate to suggest this hotel to anyone.

<Author>Del-7
<Content>Great City We stayed in the Millenium Hilton from the 29th of December through to the 8th of January. Firstly, the connections to everthing here are excellent, we took the subway to and from the airport, it only takes 45 mins not sure how long a cab takes but it is around $45, the subway is 2. The subway is also excellent for getting uptown with the 'E' dropping you right next to Macys in 34th or times square at 42nd or right up to the rockerfeller on 53rd all for 2 bucks, if your making a couple of trips a day as we did it saves alot of money on 15 - 20 buck cabs.The hotel was excellent we never had to wait long to check in and as I had requested on the hilton website when booking I got a high floor room on the 49th floor. Our room over looked ground zero out to new jersey, the view was excellent, we found that the noise was no problem unless you opened the window, though the air conditioning unit was noisy at night. The pool and sauna were nice though the buisness suite with the internet for hire was expensive, try to find an internet cafe. The only complaint I have is not to do with the hotel as such but the location I found to be a bit of a hassle, though the subway is right outside, if you were shopping up 5th avenue or in around times squre it was a bit of a trek to come back to the hotel for a change of clothes or to drop off bags etc, it was also harder to find pubs and resteraunts within walking distance.Overall though i would definatly recommend the hotel.

<Author>Marge246
<Content>Efficient, priced to compete, stylish rooms We chose the Millenium Hilton for our weekend in NYC because our rate, which included two breakfasts AND one night of champagne, was about $150 cheaper than the celestial rates of Times Square / Midtown properties WITHOUT breakfast.We were worried that being so far downtown would make transportation difficult, but with a subway station across the street, we had no problem most of the time; Saturday night cabs were scarce and the hotel only had one doorman on, so we left the long taxi line and hoofed up one block to catch our own - no big deal.We appreciated other TripAdvisor guest photos of the site, as it is across the street from the WTC site - the hotel itself was damaged in the 9/11 attacks and was closed for 18 months. (Now beautifully restored - no issues). The bellman told us a harrowing story of the day of the attack and his subsequent 9 hour walk home to the Bronx. This location, then, becomes a positive - the staff are happy to see you and grateful for your business, and you can walk a few steps out the door to see the moving WTC display or explore St. Paul's chapel, the 18thC church which miraculously survived the collapse of the towers.The room was better appointed than most brands, with a huge, flat-screen TV and glass and wood furniture. Room a little on the small side for two women who spent three days shopping, but then again, what hotel room would have held all the bags? OUTSTANDING bed.Our room overlooked WTC site, and the other side of the hotel overlooks the Brooklyn Bridge. Overall a very pleasant experience.

<Author>MontrealMember
<Content>Wonderful Hotel but a Couple of Negatives I booked 2 quad-accupancy rooms for a group of us who headed down to NYC for the Labour Day long weekend. The hotel itself has an upscale feel to it and has one of the fastest elevators I have ever experienced.Both rooms were located on the east side of the building, facing town hall and the Brooklyn Bridge, although the later is only visible from the highest floors and were not visible to us (31st and 32nd floors). The rooms were well appointed, spacious and the large-screen plasma TVs made viewing a pleasure.Several of the group has stayed mid-town on previous trips and enjoyed staying downtown, away from the hordes of tourists congregating in Time Square, Central Park and 5th Av. However, it is a ghost-town after all the white collars head home on Friday, giving it somewhat of a depressing feel when you are the only soul out walking around in the early morning or late evening. Its location across from Ground Zero doesn't really help much either... For all of the compliments, we did have two complaints. First, for a quad-occupancy room, beds were very small, making for an intimate sleeping encounter whether you wanted it or not. If you want the possibility of moving around without falling out of the bed (or accidently knocking your partner out), better upgrade to a junior suite.Secondly, because of flight delays, one of our group arrived at the hotel after our party had already headed uptown. Although the front desk assured us that it would be no problem to provide her access to the room in our absence, it turned out to be a different story. Only after half an hour and three attempts did they finally provide her with an access key.All in all, a wonderful hotel although there were several aspects which kept it from being a great stay.

<Author>TravelBugger3
<Content>Best value in NYC Wanting to get away for the weekend to NYC, we booked this hotel after many positive reviews here on tripadvisor, and I don't think we'll stay at any other NYC hotel. For the price this hotel can't be beat.Interestingly, the only downside to the hotel is its location. It's way down next to the WTC, meaning it's at the tip of southern Manhattan. But that's OK because the hotel is right outside the entranceway to the WTC subway stop on the E train. My wife and I arrived by bus at Penn Station (also on the E line), and a few stops later, was at the door to the Hilton. Plus, all the hotspots in Manhattan are served on the blue (A, C, E) line: Times Square, Columbus Circle/Central Park, Empire State Building, etc. Can't beat the convenience.Service was impeccable. We asked room service to send up toothpaste, and in timely fashion, a gentleman arrived at our door with the goods. A few minutes after that, we got a phone call from Housekeeping asking us if the toothpaste was delivered. Was a nice touch since this was the first time I had ever experienced a follow-up call, and I've stayed at many more upscale hotels.We got a king-size bedroom and as a previous poster noted, the window view was of the WTC construction site. Unlike the previous poster, I couldn't hear a thing outside our window, and we were on the 20th floor, so not too high up. Noise was not a problem.The room was a little on the small side, but that is to be expected in Manhattan. The decor was modern, and the plasma TV was a very nice touch (not to mention space saving!). The bathroom and bedsheets were all clean...no complaints.I can't speak of the restaurant or the hotel food because we didn't eat at the hotel. Why would you when the corner breakfast shop tastes better and is cheaper than any hotel fare? Just spend the day walking up broadway and you'll walk through many shops and restaurants as you pass through all the hotspots in lower Manhattan/midtown.Overall, this hotel was a real find. It was one of the cheapest hotel options in Manhattan, one of the most convenient, and we came away with no complaints about it. It's not the Ritz, the Waldorf, or the Trump, but it doesn't cost it either.

<Content>Smoker Beware Let me begin by saying we had another very nice stay at this hotel. The rooms are still small but great and the staff is very friendly and accomodating. If you are a smoker and insist on a smoking room you would be better off trying another hotel. I had reserved my smoking King room 2 months previously. Upon arrival alas there were no smoking rooms. Evidently Hilton removed a bunch of smoking floors and, of course, did not let their smoking guests know about this. There is now 1 floor that is smoking with 14 rooms on it. That means 14 out of 569 rooms are smoking rooms. Even if you book one of these rooms you are not guaranteed to get one as per the Manager of the hotel told me. The odds are pretty bad. Otherwise it's still a fine hotel. This review is just a caution to the 22% of Americans who smoke.

<Content>Not the best PROS: Very clean and comfortable rooms, friendly staff, widescreen plasma tv (no high-definition broadcasts though), very comfortable beds/pillows, excellent climate control, great view either side (if you don't mind looking at ground zero on the hudson river side [they refer to over-looking ground zero as city view]), pool and excercise room, easy subway access to everywhere.CONS:No king beds facing away from ground zero, only queen (which looked like full size), construction on ground zero 7 days a week from about 6:00 am to 3:00 pm (muffled noise), no coffee in rooms (have to go to restaurant to purchase and coffee was not good and not hot), no in-room refrigerator, charge for high-speed internet access (no wireless in rooms), walls not as sound-proof as other hotels (fine unless you have noisy people next to you or want to sleep in on ground zero side).If this hotel added a few MINOR ammenities like FREE in-room coffee and refrigerator and FREE wireless internet access, I would have felt better about the construction noise and the price. <Author>jocelynkeith
<Content>Ground Zero vista Nice price for a 4 star. Worth it to get a city view room, which is an extra $40, but puts you at least 38 floors up. Pool is indoors and on the small side. <Author>jmalder
<Content>Less than desirable We booked our hotel and was quite excited to be able to stay in Manhattan, at a four-star hotel at a Hilton hotel. Prior to check-in we had requested a king size smoking room both on the internet and by the phone. When we finally moved our way through closed streets and quite a bit of construction and got our car parked ($48.00 a day - no in and out), they did have us in a king size room but it was a non-smoking room. Supposedly they did not have a smoking room available but the gentleman at the front desk left us for a few minutes and voila! A smoking room was suddenly available. We got to our room and my husband and I were really excited to see what type of view we would have. We were able to see the Hudson and some of the skyscrapers on the financial district but the main eye-catching site was that of ground zero. It was quite depressing and bone-chilling to look out our window. Wireless internet is available at the hotel. When using the lounge near the front desk, it's $5.95 AN HOUR. In your room, it ranges from $5.95 to $9.95 for a 24 hour period. I have noticed no difference between the $5.95 and the $9.95 service so don't waste your money on the $9.95 option.The room itself is nice. The beds at their sister hotel, Hampton Inn, are a lot more comfortable. The beds have a duvet that covers it with no duvet cover. The plasma television is nice but not that big of a deal. Breakfast is not provided by the restaurant but you are able to order a continental breakfast for $18.00 plus a 15% gratuity and a $4.00 in-room dining charge. There are also no soda vending machines on any floor but you are able to purchase a fountain drink in the lounge for $3.75. It is in a good subway location. There are two subway entrances right across the street and are easily accessible. Beware of walking up Fulton Street towards Broadway or you'll get accousted by all the street vendors selling knock-off merchandise.Overall, I'm not impressed with this 4-star hotel at all. Give me the 2 1/2 star ones any day.

<Author>larasweb
<Content>Best Stay! I just returned from an over night stay at the Millenium Hilton and I have to say that it far exceeded my expectations. I did book through a discount website and so it didnt hurt that the room was 50% off of the regular rate. This was the deal of a lifetime. We scored a very spacious corner room with a great view facing north east. We had a great view. The beds were exceptionally comfortable complete with down comforters and pillows. The huge plasma TV was awesome as well. Travellers should know that the west facing side of the building directly faces ground zero. As a New Yorker who lived here during 9/11 I found the location saddening but also felt really good about staying at the hotel and contributing to the rebirth of lower Manhattan. The indoor pool (surrounded by potted palm trees) was fabulous as was the extremely courteous and helpful staff. Truth be told, I didnt want to leave! Two thumbs up!

<Author>lass=
<Content>Very good hotel, especially if you get a good rate I booked this hotel for a long weekend in July, primarily because of the many good reviews on tripadvisor.com, and I wasn't disappointed. This is mainly a business hotel, because of its location in lower Manhattan, and it costs over $300 a night during the week. You can however get some very good weekend rates: I ended up paying $189 per night plus taxes, which is very good value for a 4 star hotel in Manhattan.The room was very clean and well decorated in a modern style. The bed was very comfortable. The plasma TV was a nice touch.I was a little bit concerned that the location would be dead on the weekend, but there were several good deli-style cafes in the area for brunch. The open-top tour buses stop right beside the hotel and the Staten Island ferry terminal, Brooklyn Bridge and Battery Park are all pretty close. The subway is right by the hotel and I did take quite a few taxis to other parts of Manhattan, which were plentiful and not too expensive.I did order room service one night after midnight and the sandwiches and burger we received were OK but very expensive.The staff were friendly and efficient on check-in and check-out.I would recommend this hotel for a weekend visit to New York, if the price is right.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Stay over weekend at the Millenium First thing which immediately became obvious was the roadworks outside causing issues with actually getting into the hotel. Once there though I was met by polite reception staff and bag was whisked up to my run. I'd been upgraded to a room on the 48th floor. Interior of rooms have certainly been upgraded since last time I came to the millenium. Large plasma screen tv was nice touch. Contemporary furniture beginning to look a little dated already. Small/average size of room for Manhatten. I travel on business to NY frequently and the hotel is respectable but certainly not my first choice for a stay, however it has improved since refurb work

<Author>sannicandrob
<Content>Great Views, Nice Hotel too! We arrived on a Saturday for a weekend stay at the Millenium Hilton. They are doing construction on Church Street, so you are forced to enter through the side entrance on Fulton Street. This particular trip we drove into NYC, and it was POURING rain. I couldn't have asked for a more helpful staff as we arrived. We had our two small children with us, so the bellman immediately came to my car and started grabbing my bags. He was so fast, I had to slow him down, so he didn't bring all the contents of my car into the hotel. It was great service. He encouraged us to get the kids inside and had my car valet parked. I had my room keys within a few minutes and my bags were taken up to my room with us. The rooms were clean and comfortable, but not huge - typical of NYC. Flat screen tv was great for the kids, but reception wasn't that spectacular for some channels. The view from the 28th floor over former WTC site is unreal, even in the rain! The lobby was small, but nice. The gift shop was the size of a closet. Once four people get in there, it gets complicated. Most importantly, all staff members I encountered at this hotel were friendly. The concierge was very helpful in recommending nearby eateries that would suit our budget, and accomodate two small kids. He knew everything from local pizzerias and delis to 5 star restaurants. The subway was right across the street, and also a block away (depending on what line you were looking for) so we were able to access all of NYC very easily. The rates at this hotel tend to be pretty high whenver I check them, but because of its location, it tends to be much less expensive on the weekends. Give it a shot! My one negative of the visit was when I picked up my car from the valet. It's a Hilton garage right behind the hotel, but it's operated by a parking lot company. You have to call a number from your room to tell them you want your car, as it takes up to 1/2 hour for them to get your car. We were never told of that, until after the bellman came up to get our bags. We were told to wait in the lobby and ended up doing so for quite some time. Then our car was brought out and nobody told us it was ready. It was pretty confusing. Other than that minor mishap, I'd say this hotel was worth the price I paid.  
<Date>Jun 3, 2006

<Author>mimicatl
<Content>Great Location/Amenities...Just In The Budget We usually stay at more independent hotels when we go to New York for two reasons; usually a lot more inexpensive and predictable on the amenities/service (once you've found a good one). This trip was somewhat last minute and we looked at all of our usual locales and came up with nothing. The Millennium Hilton looked appealing because it was basically the same price as less than stellar comparables and it was right by all of the subway lines we needed.Bottom line...we were blown away by the quality of the rooms, service, and location. It's basically a 4 star hotel in my opinion for NYC. Across the street from the WTC site its within blocks of almost all subway lines (W,Q,N,E,C,B,etc.). Would definitely stay there again if we could get the same deal (around $200), but have a feeling that its cheap only because of all of the construction going on in the area.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Very nice hotel We travel frequently to NYC, and stay at Hilton hotels, as I am a frequent business traveler and all of my stays have been reward stays.The Millenium was the fourth hotel in NYC that we tried. It was very clean, and indeed had plasma screen tv's as advertised. Twice we have stayed in the Time Square area, and it was very noisy in the room (New York Hilton). The traffic down in lower Manhattan is inconsequential and subsequently, we slept great. The bed is very comfortable, and the bathroom is average size. Overall, a nice hotel. The lobby isn't fancy, which I don't have a problem with, since at this hotel they used the money they saved and put it in the hotel rooms.If you're concerned about staying in a location that's not central, not too worry. The subway is right across the street, and cabs are readily available all hours of the day. A cab ride to the Rockerfeller Center area will run you about $10, a Lincoln Town Car about $25 - $30.I would definately stay at this hotel again.

<Author>Girloadventure
<Content>The secret's out, this is the place to stay in NYC! My husband had stayed here many times for business so he suggested it for a recent weekend trip with family and it turned out to be a good deal (from Hilton web site, we paid under $200 a night which isn't bad in NYC) and a nice place to stay. Note: if you want to hang out and wave at the TV cameras in Times Square, that is not even within walking distance. Not near Broadway, either. This hotel is in the financial district, right across from where the World Trade Center towers once stood. Convenient to subway. Lots of cabs around.The room was small and modern and very clean but the view was awesome -- we were on a corner so we could look out at Ground Zero and the new building underway plus see out to the water and across to Brooklyn. Battery Park is within walking distance (wonderful views, can go to Ellis Island and Statute of Liberty from here. The tulips were blooming and we people watched the joggers and doggies and such). Also close are SoHo, TriBecca and Chinatown. Century 21 is next door to the hotel and JR Music World is nearby. Fewer tourists and what a relief to be away from the zoo that is Times Square but the hotel was full when we stayed so don't expect to have the place for yourself on a weekend (bummer!) The Crabtree and Evelyn bath products are nice. Breakfast buffet had 2 kinds of eggs, suasage, bacon, fresh fruit, cereals, granola, French toast, wonderful pastries and bagels and more that I am simply not remembering. It was free due to H's Diamond status but they charge $20 ordinarily. Fear not: there are several Starbucks nearby as well as many other options. Front desk and housekeeping staffs were courteous and efficient. We'd booked online and everything was smooth -- we needed 2 rooms, one a handicapped accessible and that was not a problem. Though we booked separately, we made a note online and they did put rooms together. Only negative: the dining room staff are very uneven. They can be awful (i.e. neglectful about refills and even snotty of attitude. Sometimes you will stand and wait for a table for several minutes though half the restaurant is empty and many staff are milling around). Then the next morning, they will be prompt, courteous and great. They have some weird hierarchy they try to impose on the window seats -- don't let them. If youwant to sit by a window and there is one open, tell them when they seat you and don't take any silliness. They are also sloppy about the bill so check the check!! Overall, a great stay. We will be back.  
<Date>May 3, 2006

<Author>rcr86
<Content>Good Value Last weekend I spent 2 nights at this hotel with a few friends from out of town for St Patricks Day weekend. The stay started out a little rocky since we were told that our car would be parked off site and we would not have access to it for the duration of our visit. I am guessing this is not uncommon in NYC, but still inconvienent. Then, when we checked in we were told at registration that the room had only one bed! This was unacceptable since there were 4 of us and my reservation had specifically stated that I had reserved a room with 2 beds. After assuring us that there were no rooms with two beds in the entire hotel (suites included) for nearly 10 minutes, they magically found one on the 42nd floor. I have to say they were pleasant during this entire process but it took some major patience and negotiating to resolve. Once these initial snafus were past us, the rest of the weekend was a blast! The room was immaculate and well stocked with towels and glasses and provided an impressive view uptown and of the Hudson. The cleaning staff did a excellent job and the concierge and bellman were all eager to help us enjoy our stay.The hotel location is in the Financial District so it tended to get a little quiet at night (it's no Times Square). However, there is a nice subway station at Ground Zero right in front of the hotel and taxi service from the side door (the actual front entrance was under construction while we were there). We found it easy to get anywhere from this hotel by using either the train ($2/per person) or getting a cab (usually less than $10). The only real gripe I have with the stay is that the room got really hot after the first night and there was no effective way to cool it down. Only one small section of our window would open and even then it only moved about 2 inches. It was 34 degrees out but our room constantly hovered around 80 degrees with the A/C on. The front desk said that their HVAC system was based on hot water so when it is heating season, there is no A/C and vice versa. This seems pretty archaic to me so, to future winter travelers I would recommend keeping a window open since you can always heat up the room if necessary.Overall the stay was good and we had a wonderful experience. I would definitely stay here again.PS Our beautiful 42 plasma TV was hobbled by a poor cable feed that created a crappy picture.  
<Date>Mar 22, 2006

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Quality hotel with hidden supprises Just got back after a long weekend in the Big Apple with my wife.We decided on the Millennium Hilton because of the good price that was on offer when we booked through Expedia, plus I didn't fancy staying in a midtown hotel.Overall I have to say that the service at this hotel was some of the best I have had at a 4*+ hotel. The staff would answer the phone after on ring and there was always someone to hand on the main desk.The rooms were large by New York standards, we had a King deluxe suite, and were well appointed with high speed internet access, plenty of stationary, Crabtree  Evelyn bath products, digital climate control, three setting power shower and the infamous 42 plasma screen. The standard king size The Bed is one of the most comfortable beds I have stayed in and was well received after all the walking we did.As for the view, we were on the 21st floor and we had a fabulous view of the Hudson River. As for the view of Ground Zero, whilst it is sobering the first time you see it from up high you quickly realise that New York and its residents have moved on and won't let it get the better of them and soon you feel the same way.I read in a previous review about the Stage Door Deli located on Vesey Street. This place serves up some of the best Hero's in New York at very reasonable prices. The breakfast is bigger, nicer and 1/3 of the price in the hotel.The swimming pool and sauna is a nice addition and like the bed is very welcome after a long day out.Century 21 located next door is a must. I picked up a pair of Hugo Boss jeans for $90 reduced from $180. There are bargains all over the store and the place is busy all day with long queues for the changing rooms.Now for the hidden surprise.Hilton charges a fee of $75 per night to cover incidentals. This is deducted from your credit card when you check in. If, like myself, you rely on you credit card it can come as a surprise when your card is rejected. As with European hotels your credit card details are taken when you check in but instead of assessing any costs and deducting them from your card when you check out, they deduct $75 per night there and then. They do not tell you that they will deduct it straight away nor is it explained in any of their literature. I was told that it did explain on the Hilton website but as I did not book through their website I did not read this. I tried to get the money back after the embarrassment of having my card refused only to be told that because it was the weekend they couldn't do anything until the Monday. Now as this was on a Saturday it left us with little money and forced us to eat and drink at the hotel. So make sure you have this covered. Also beware of what the bellboys call a taxi. Out side the hotel will be rows of black cars/limos. Whilst they are licensed by the TLC they operate a fixed rate and not metered. We took one of these cars from the hotel to the Empire State building and it cost us $24 (without tip) where as the taxi back cost $15 (including tip). However, these cars come in handy going back to JFK because the fixed rate is $50 regardless of how long it takes to get there whereas a taxi is on a meter and it took us nearly an hour to get to the airport at 2pm.  
<Date>Feb 8, 2006

<Author>Anonymus
<Content>Fantastic trip! My husband and I took my parents to the Millenium Hilton for a long weekend. At first we were nervous after reading the other reviews; however, the hotel was wonderful! The location was excellent. You were a 15-20 minute walk to Soho and Little Italy. The Statue of Liberty was close by too. The hotel bar (in the lobby) was expensive, but there are plenty of watering holes to visit. The train was literally across the street from the WTC complex. As for the location being depressing...If you plan on staying at a hotel across the street from the worst terrorist attack of our generation then you should expect to be moved. It made you stop and reflect; however, it was hardly depressing.The rooms were clean, clean and clean. I am used to staying at the Ritz Carlton Battery Park. These rooms are smaller, but for the value, the location and quality of the hotel far exceeds the Ritz.The only complaint was obtaining the car from the parking garage. I recommend calling one hour prior to pick-up (especially if checking out at noon), there was a delay in getting the car.Do not hesitate to stay here.

<Author>buddyandme
<Content>Beautiful hotel but some service issues Stayed at the Hilton Millenium for three nights Jan. 3-6 2006. Stayed on the 54th floor in a king parlor corner suite. I doubt there could be better views from any room in any hotel in NYC. Hudson River to the west, with magnificent sunsets. East River to the east with beautiful views of Brooklyn Bridge. Out the center windows Ground Zero and beyond. The views at night were the most beautiful with buildings and bridges sparkling in all three directions. The room was wonderful. Seperate bedroom with master bath including seperate shower and tub. Large living area with couches, chairs, and dining table. Our daughters slept on pull out sofa and had their own bath. Could not have asked for a nicer suite for our family.Service issues-room not ready when we arrived so desk clerk told us baggage handlers would store baggage. Much appreciated. Asked concierge who to arrange this with and they continued their joking and laughing and pointed toward bellmen. Asked a bellman and he pointed to another bellman. That bellman held up his hand to me to stop my request mid-sentence, informed me he was helping somebody else. Poor customer service. Room service was slow, expensive, and the food was poor. Twice attempted to get something from gift shop and both times found sign on the door be right back. If not for these issues, could be a five star hotel.Saw two shows, Wicked and The Producers. Both were great. Exhibit at South St. Sea Port called Bodies amazing and should not be missed. Human cadavers donated to science have been treated,preserved, and displayed to allow people to see bones,muscles,organs,pathological conditions such as a brain that has suffered a stroke, smokers vs. non-smokers lung etc. This was done with taste and dignity. A great educational experience. The Stage Deli, as always has the best deli food and enormous, well worth the calories desserts. The Stage Door Deli across from the Millenium Hilton is not related, not really that good, and there was a mouse running around between tables when we were there. Would have been nice to have in room coffee but Starbucks and bagels just around the corner. China town great fun and great food. Great city, great trip, and great hotel suite. Would stay again despite service issues because suite and views so nice.  
<Date>Jan 14, 2006

<Author>brum1955
<Content>It does exactly what it says on the label No doubting its a very good hotel. But...it IS a Hilton and had we not had the view over Ground Zero we could have been in a Hilton Hotel in any number of large cities.At least you know what you are getting.Special mention has to go to Joe one of the concierge, and Steve one of the Doormen. Excellent service above and beyond. Joe managed to get us booked into a New Years Eve Dinner Dance at a restaurent within 5 mins walk of the hotel at less that 24hr notice and it was fantastic value at $150 for two inc 4 courses + live music + an open bar 9-12pm. Steve managed to get us an immaculate stretched limo for our trip to see Fiddler on the Roof at just $35 door to door!! Thanks guys.The extortionate prices of the hotels breakfast ($22pp) can easily be avoided.There ARE a number of good restaurants and deli/diners for that authentic NYC breakfast or brunch in the Financial District.The Stage Door Deli / Essex Cafe and Paninis are all within a few hundred metres and offer great value for money and are recommended both for food quality and that edgy NYC atmosphere.For dinner we would heartily recommend Giovanni's Atrium ( Italian ) and Les Halles ( French ) both exellent and again within easy walking distance. O'Haras Bar/Restaurant next to the Fire Station adjacent to Ground Zero is 'ok' but couldn't be recommended, pretty basic food and service, and not that cheap. Worth seeing/doing while you are there?USS Intrepid,Circle Line Boat Trip,Central Park etc. At the Empire State Building, avoid the queues and buy the virtual flight tickets off the guys in the yellow jackets who will offer you tickets while you are in the queue for the Empire. Sure its a few extra dollars but it will save you anything up to a 3 to 4hr wait. Another alert! We bought a City Pass book for a number of attractions prior to going. It states in the City Pass that it allows you to beat the queues and go straight to the front of the line....it doesn't work, you will be directed to joint the queue at the back just like everyone else.National History Museum adjacent to Central Park.It's good BUT probably needs at least two days to do it justice. Cabs were an total lottery. We had the full spectrum from a genuine new yorker type ( a la De Niro )who was great. The other end of the scale was an atrocious driver of far eastern origin who it seemed had little or no idea of geography or driving skills and even decided to stop for petrol and take a leak while the meter was left running and added about $3 to the bill...bizarre.For real night time entertainment either head for Chinatown ( Winnies is fun, although not for the faint hearted ). Swing46 a really cool Jazz Bar/Restaurant on 46th Street offers a great value fixed price 3 course meal for $22 before 7.30pm, ideal for pre theatre eats. Just along the street from there is a great piano/singalong bar where you will be entertained by Broadway singers for the price of your beers. The Oyster Bar on the lower level at Grand Central Station should not be missed.New York really is spectacular.  Overall a great 50th Birthday trip. I just need a holday to get over it now!!!!!  
<Date>Jan 4, 2006

<Author>Annie40
<Content>GREAT HOTEL WITH FANTASTIC VIEWS I stayed at this hotel with my husband and two children (aged 9  13) over Xmas and New Year. We had a corner room on the 45th floor with large windows overlooking Ground Zero and The Statue of Liberty on one side and Brooklyn  Manhattan Bridge on the other side. The room was large enough for the four of us and bigger than most I have stayed in across Europe. The only thing we would have liked in the room is tea  coffee making facilities, but they did provide bottled water in the room every day at no cost. The indoor pool was a real bonus for us as the children enjoyed a swim after a long days sightseeing. All the hotel staff were very helpful and friendly. Getting to Midtown was very easy, a taxi outside the hotel cost between $10- $15. The Subway was another option and cost $2 each or you could buy a pass making it cheaper per trip. You can get a really good breakfast at The Stage Door Deli across the road. On a previous trip I stayed in Times Square at The Marriott Marquis, which was equally as nice but did not have a pool. I would recommend this hotel to anyone wanting a good quality hotel with a pool who doesn't mind getting a taxi or Subway into Midtown (takes about 20 mins).We went to Central Park on New Years Eve and saw some amazing fireworks and a midnight run.

<Author>polarbear123
<Content>Nice Hotel We stayed at the Millenium Hilton on December 3. The prices were high throughout New York since it was prime shopping season. We chose to stay here as it seemed like the nicest hotel for the money. I booked through the Hilton website about 1 month prior to our visit. In the final week the price dropped $200. I called the hotel to ask for an adjustment and they accomdated me quite politely. Be sure to watch the prices as your date gets closer!The hotel overall was nice. The room was on the small side, but from what I hear this is typical. It was very clean and comfortable. Our room was over looking Ground Zero. As my husband put it, if you could throw a rock out the window you would hit it. It was a distance from Midtown but the cabs were always available.Overall we enjoyed our stay here and would consider it again.

<Author>MaggieJones
<Content>Very enjoyable - just a couple of minus points My husband and I stayed in this hotel for 5 nights late December. Our room was very pleasant and comfortable. <Author>ShawnH
<Content>Didn't care for it I just joined this great site and felt I owed a post.First of all, I found the location depressing. This hotel is like a NYC sliver building, and every window overlooks what is essentially a mass grave. Its a bizarre, alienating experience to walk around in your skivvies as your room seems to positively overhang this great, grey chasm.Speaking of windows, seemed to me the building was redone rather shabbily after 9/11, and the curtain wall exterior is too thin and lets in too much noise. I had to change rooms because one of the enormous windows was flexing and popping in the wind.Lastly, don't pay extra for a suite unless you really need a separate office. From what I can see, a suite gets you pretty much the same floor space as a standard room, only chopped into two too-small roomlets by placing the bathroom between. If you do stay, the standard room is nicer.

<Author>lillious
<Content>ok, not great My family of 6 spent 2 nights (thanksgiving) at this Hilton. The lobby is very small by HIlton standards. Check in was smooth. Got to the room to find that the double beds were smaller than standard size. So we called to the front desk to order roll aways. No problem, $25 per bed per room. Yikes! Our sons room mini fridge was full of old and smelly food. Housekeeping came up quickly to remove. Later that evening I called for more washcloths as there was only 1 in our room. An hour later they were delivered. Plasma screen tvs don't impress me like they seem to impress so many other guests. tv is tv. We go to NYC to see the sights not watch things we can watch at home. Exercise facilities and pool are very nice. Having to pay for internet service is ridiculous! I find it funny that Hampton Inn's don't charge for internet service and yet the more upscale Hilton properties try to grab more money from you for something that should easily be included in your hotel quote.Location of this Hilton is only a minor inconvenience. Subway is just across the street and taxis are plentiful. Valet parking only at $45 per night. No in and out parking available. Takes about 25 mintues to get your car.Had desert in the hotel restaurant. Very good and staff was very friendly. Breakfast was suppose to be included but my husband had to go to the front desk to have the charges removed.Being across the street from the World Trade Center site was humbling and my family spent some time just looking out our windows at the site as well as walking around the area.No real perks at this Hilton for belonging to Hilton Honors. Would I choose this Hilton again, probably not. I wouldn't mind the distance to main sights if the hotel itself was more appealing. We have stayed in many hotels in NYC that had more ambience. However, if you get a good rate and it's price you are interested in than you'll probably be okay here.

<Author>rkachur
<Content>Millenium Hilton - a great option After struggling to find a hotel room under $250, I finally used priceline and got the Millenium Hilton for $200/night. I would definitely recommend this hotel. From what I understand the majority of the rooms have king-sized beds and views of ground zero, which also means views of the Hudson river. My husband and I didn't come here to see ground zero but rather to visit with friends but this hotel is perfectly located for those doing the touristy thing. It's close to the subway (1,9, A, C, E) and directly across the street from the PATH train. The area has everything you would need - coffee shops, shopping, etc. I expected downtown to be desolate but it isn't. The hotel is very clean and the rooms have recently been renovated. Although the rooms are probably typical NYC size (small) they are so well-designed that you hardly realize it. Our room had a plasma tv, a sleek desk with internet access, a sitting chair, a king sized bed and huge windows looking out over NY. The bathroom was huge and had big towels and crabtree  evelyn products. The only bummer was that there was not a coffee maker in our room so we had to schlep downstairs to get some. We also made the mistake of eating breakfast in the hotel restaurant one morning. Although it was good, it cost us $20/person. Pretty hefty when we could have crossed the street and gotten the same thing for half the price. Overall, I would stay here again in a heartbeat and would recommend this hotel to anyone visiting NYC.

<Author>SueFee
<Content>A Really Nice Hotel! In our previous visits to New York City, we've always stayed in midtown Manhattan. However, when our usual hotel was booked solid, we decided to give the Millenium Hilton a try---and we were glad we did! We paid about $30/night extra for a room on the 31st-55th floor and got one on the 35th floor. The view is bittersweet---great city and Jersey views but sad at the same time since you are reminded of what used to be across the street.  The hotel is very clean and housekeeping is excellent--very consistent. Every night we were there, they had turn-down service. Not only did they turn down the bedcovers but they filled the ice bucket and left two bottles of water and two pieces of chocolate. As others pointed out, the toiletries are nice---Crabtree and Evelyn. The flat-screen plasma TV is nice, too. The only problem with that is the way it's positioned, you need to sit on the bed to see it or position the desk chair so that it faces the TV. We found the bed to be very comfortable and even though we were near the elevator and ice machine, we never had a problem with noise. The closet is small but it met our needs just fine. Elevator service is great--prompt and fast--we never had a problem with that. At this hotel, you are very close to several subway lines so getting around the city is quite easy.  We didn't eat at the hotel restaurant since there are so many other options available in NYC. Plus, you can get a much cheaper breakfast elsewhere. In short, we would gladly stay here again! While we would have preferred a room on the other side of the hotel, we discovered that only the suites and junior suites face in the other direction---so it would have been more expensive.  
<Date>Oct 2, 2005

<Author>karissa2000
<Content>Best Hotel I've Ever Stayed In!!! I stayed at this hotel from September 2nd - September 5th, for Labor Day Weekend. I reserved months in advance, so i was able to book for $199 per night. For the three nights it came up to about $690, which was well worth the stay. For an easy way to get here from Newark International, you can catch the #62 bus to Newark Penn Station which is $1.50. Then catch the Path Train to the World Trade Center Path Station. The cost of the ticket is also $1.50. As you come out of the train station the hotel is right across the street. How convenient is that. The view was amazing. I was in Room 1704. Having a city view, you're looking straight down into the World Trade Center. The area is close to alot of restaurants and its a short walk down to Battery Park for the statue of liberty. Another site not to miss is South Side Seaport which is just a few blocks away as well. You're situated right infront of Bradway, soo you;re close to many restaurants. TGI Fridays is right out the door. There;s also Century 21 right next door, which is a department store which sells discount name brand items.The two best things about his hotel is their restaurant and the plasma TV. The rooms are extremely clean and you'll feel like King and Queen. For anyone having dinner at Church and Dey Restaurant, the food is great. Their steak is the softest i've ever tasted. But my all-time favourite is the lemon chicken with mashed potatoes. Up til now i cant stop thinking about how great those mashed potatoes are.This hotel is the best that i've ever stayed in and the service is excellent. I will always stay here as long as i'm i New York.Warning: Don't touch anything in the mini bar. And i mean TOUCH! You'll be charged, and they're not exactly cheap!

<Author>seamus266
<Content>A+ Hotel, A+ Location, A+ View, A+ Value Arrived via Amtrak from Phiadelphia at 1PM Sept. 9 for a 3 night stay.Despite being early check-in, they had a room on the 45th floor ready and awaiting my arrival. First, realize this hotel is downtown, near Wall St. and immediately across the street from Ground Zero. Built in the early 1990's, the hotel was damaged by the scumbags, closed for nearly 2 years, and completely re-vamped. I stayed in the regular 1King bed room. This is the most basic room at the hotel. For more $ you can get a junior suite, which offers some more room, and a view that looks more uptown rather than downtown. Some consider this a plus. For me, ground zero, the buildings around ground zero, the Hudson River with its traffic, and NJ and the sunsets made my view the best in the hotel. All rooms offer the large plasma TV, nice work table with convenient internet and electrical plugs, floor to ceiling windows and in-room safe. No in-room wireless internet (wireless in lobby/lounge/restaurant only). They charge $5.95 per 24 hours, or $9.95 if you must log on to your own internet provider. They will give you the T1 cord for a $10 deposit.Rooms very comfortable. Bed nice and well appointed with sheets and comforter. Closet small-enough room for 1 person but would be stretching it for 2 people. The dresser is dominated by mini-bar, mini-refer which doesn't leave a lot of drawer space. Bathrooms very nice w/marble and a good shower up high so someone 6'2 or so doesn't have to bend over to wash hair. Towels and bathroom amenities servicable. Note only one sink-may be 2 in the junior suite - if that's an issue, check.Not only is the room comfortable and new, the view is stunning. I was there for the 911 aniversary/memorial. To look out and see the crowds and the firetrucks and police cars and mourners and everyone else paying their respects was staggering. To be able to walk out the door and across the street and be Right There was amazing. A lot of people suggest staying up towards ( or in) Times Square so you can really be a part of the party. I disagree and am more than happy I stayed at the M. Hilton. 15 minute walk to L.Italy/Chinatown. 15 to Wall St. 15 to ferry boats to NJ. Anything further, there is a subway stop a block away, or just catch a cab. It is quieter and less congested down here than up at Times Sq. It is convenient to go up in the evening, see Times, see the lights and masses of people and hawkers, and for me; cool to leave it behind and come back to the hotel. Also, restaurant and room service both very good - if you do get room service, realize you are paying $4 plus 15% on top of the price of food. This is the tip. Don't leave more money after you are already forced to tip (unless you are just really generous - if so, give me a call). I had no time for pool and no need for work-out after all the hiking I did each day, so I can not comment on either of those facilities. My minor complaint: while room was clean, there were a couple strands of hair in tub. I seem to see this almost everywhere I stay, yet I don't like it and find it disquieting - once I see that I question the cleanliness of the rest of the room and am on the lookout for something else to complain about. Other very minor incident - on 9/11 I removed DND sign from door and went to GZ. Returned 2 hrs. later and room not yet cleaned. Called housekeeping then took computer down to lounge, had a drink, sent a couple emails, returned 50 minutes later, and room was completed. No big deal.I will certainly stay at the Millenium Hilton again. In fact, I am already planning my next trip in 2006 to NYC, and have no cause to stay anywhere else. Last advice, if you do stay at a Hilton property, become a member of their frequent guest club. 500 miles per stay or a couple other options. If you like to fly first class you can't beat incentive bonuses.

<Author>PT1976
<Content>Clean, comfortable, and Great staff Booked a room on hotwire for $202 (174 + tax) a few days before our Friday night visit. We called a day earlier to ask if we could check in at noon and receptionist was frosty, said she couldn't guarantee anything. Arrival was easy; there's an ACE and 123 stop (Chambers St) just steps from the hotel. We arrived at noon and the front desk clerk was gracious and accomodating and found us a room on the 41st floor facing the world trade center site and the river. Great views. Decor was generic but the bed was comfortable and linens pristine. Bathroom was decently sized, had a nice tub, Crabtree and Evelyn toiletries, and a shaving mirror. This was definitely a nice business-type hotel. Location was perfect for us because we prefer downtown and it was nice to be close to Brooklyn where our friends live. Cons included lack of decent food (except a deli) around the corner. Plus, this part of the city is quieter and you can get anywhere in minutes using the subway. Front desk was exceptionally friendly and helpful - they are what makes this place stand out.
