<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Millenium Hilton - You Can't Go Wrong Here !! I read all the reviews with skepticism. I've been disappointed before with New York hotels. This time, however, I was not. From the moment you walk off the sidewalk, you realize this hotel is upscale. The location is incredible: right across the street from the World Trade Center plaza and in walking distance to many attractions. There are also several wonderful restaurants within a few blocks. Be sure to check out St. Paul's Chapel right next door. It was built in 1766 and has a cemetary on the grounds with stones dating back to the 1700's. George Washington has a special pew in the church. This was a resting spot for the volunteers in the 9/11 tragedy and there is a lot of memorabilia and photos on display. A must-see. But get there early - as I recall visiting hours end around 3 p.m.As for the hotel, the rooms are not large, but they are very comfortable and extremely clean. The beds are superb with down comforters, and each room has a large flat panel television. The hotel is well constructed and the rooms are quiet. The only noise you will hear is the plumbing, but I doubt there is anything that could be done about that. As you might expect, the food here is expensive. I only had the breakfast buffet (once), but it set me back around $20. Pricey by anyone's standards.The views are incredible. I stayed on the 23rd floor and had a perfect view straight down into ground zero. It really made me reflect on the heroism shown and the lives lost in that tragedy. The service at this hotel is also superb. I felt like the staff went out of their way to make sure everything was perfect. From the front desk to the bellmen, they were all just top-notch.I paid $389 per night, which would be exorbitant in any other city in the country, but I felt like I got my money's worth here. I stayed here three nights in late August, and I'll not hesitate to stay here again when I return to New York.

<Content>Great...for the price! My husband and I stayed here after having camped in the Adirondaks for a few days. This was to be the pampering part of our vacation...2 nights in New York! <Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Wonderful Experience - Exceptional Customer Service Even a New Yorker should get away for the weekend! I was impressed from the moment I entered the lobby of the Millenium Hilton,. Although I live in NYC, I took avantage of a great rate to experience the hotel for a special anniversary weekend. As Hilton HHonors Gold VIP members, we were secretly crossing out fingers for an upgrade. We were quite lucky, as we were placed in a junior suite with incredible views, even at a relatively low floor! I had expressed in the comments during my reservation that we were staying there to celebrate our anniversary, and I can honestly say that I am impressed that they not only read the comments I had submitted, but actually wished us a happy anniversary! This may be small, but a time and age (and city) where your reservation is either a number or a last name, a personal touch such as that is quite unusual and highly appreciated. Although I know the standard benefits for Gold VIP members staying at US Hilton hotels calls for either a room upgrade or complimentary breakfast, depending upon availability, I was happily surprised when we were also given two certificates for full American breakfasts (a normally ridiculous $22/person value!).The layout of the junior suite is quite nice, the bathroom space creating a small hallway to separate the living space from the bedroom area. The entire space is pretty compact, but never feels small, due to the large windows and well organized furniture. The king bed was extremely comfortable. Having a corner view of the city behind our 42inch plasma television, we couldn鈥檛 have been happier. We spent some time sitting near the window just looking out at familiar buildings and streets, all from a new angle.Our breakfast buffet was very good (it seems worth the $22 when it鈥檚 free!). As usual, we requested a late checkout of around 1pm, which they graciously offered to us. All in all, I was very impressed by the level of customer service and professionalism of the staff. The building itself was gorgeous in its design, elegant details, and modern feel. The room was not only a sweet surprise, but was furnished with high quality materials and the new 鈥淟a Source鈥?bath products by Crabtree  Evelyn. Having said that, I would definitely recommend this hotel to anyone in the area, should the downtown location not be a hassle for them. The rates seem (generally) cheaper than the other Hilton properties on the island (even the Hampton Inn鈥檚) and the level of service is truly worth the deal. With all of the reviews I read before hand, I was anticipating my upcoming stay with nothing but excitement, and now that I am here typing up my own review, I look back upon my weekend with nothing but compliments to give to the Millenium Hilton. (Check out my other reviews, including: Hilton Montreal/Laval, Hilton Southbury, CT, Hilton Garden Inn Westbury, NY, Hampton Inn Somerset, PA, Homewood Suites Farmington, CT)

<Author>foursquarebar
<Content>Sleek, stylish, great subway location Got a corner king city-view room for just under $300 a night, after taxes, which was not too bad considering the good location, convenience, and *amazing* city view from the room. We usually stay in Midtown and enjoyed being away from the congestion of that area. The sleek black tower was easy to find and next to the WTC site. St. Paul's Church right beside the hotel has some compelling exhibits and stories about 9/11 inside and a very old graveyard that is beautiful and parklike. Good shopping is close by too. My spouse was duly impressed for his 40th birthday. Furnishings are modern, and wow did he love the flat screen tv on the wall. Nice beds too. (I continue to *hate* the fridge with the hugely marked-up items and no room for your own soda or water.) In NYC, you don't spend too much time in the room, but we had a chance to enjoy a bottle of wine while gazing out over Manhattan at night, lovely! We appreciated the wine glasses and corkscrew in the room, and I liked the Crabtree  Evelyn toiletries.We did not take advantage of the pool, the lobby bar, or the Church  Dey restaurant, too many other things to do. We did notice that there was wireless in the bar and restaurant, and the lobby bar always seemed busy. My husband is a huge subway fan and loved our central location for getting just about any train we needed, from Midtown to Coney Island. The location is extremely convenient. I'd stay here again in a regular room if I could get some of the under-$200 prices that others seem to be snagging. Normally, I go budget, but this place came through for me when I needed a special occasion room without seeing it first. I will continue to wonder why this hotel spells its own name wrong. Don't let that steer you away. :-)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Stay---though out of the way for tourists My wife and I spent six nights at the Millenium Hilton during our first ever stay in New York City. We were on an award stay from Hilton, and they put us in a very nice 25th floor two-room suite over looking Ground Zero---which can only be described as a sobering view. Because of our frequent travel status, we did receive free breakfast coupons, which were great because the breakfast buffet (while very good) costs roughly $25 a head. There are a bunch of places within walking distance for breakfast and lunch, though you will find your dinner options a little limited.The room was very clean and upscale. The beds were quite comfortable, and the sitting room had a fridge, work area, and separate sitting area. The bathroom had a great shower, and the bedroom had a very large flat screen television.If anyone in your crowd likes to shop, the hotel is located right next door to Century 21---which for those of you from the south, is a little like a Steinmart or TJ Maxx on steriods. The only downside, at least for those of us in the tourist crowd, is the location of the hotel compared to midtown attractions. You are a $12-15 cab ride, or a pretty lengthy subway ride to midtown---even more if you are going to the museums on either the upper east or upper west side. Many could see this as a positive, since this hotel is in a very quiet part of town.On the upside, however, you are within a block of two very large subway stations, from which you can catch nearly any of the major lines. The subway is very easy to use, though if you catch a local train, it is probably a 15-25 minute ride into midtown---and you will want to cab it back to this hotel if you come back late at night. Finally, leaving the hotel is quite easy. The bell station arranged all of our travel back to the airport, and actually found us a town car that cost us less than our cab ride in to town.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect Views, Wonderful NYC Retreat! We traveled by train from Washington DC to New York on the weekend of July 28th. We had requested an early check-in but when we arrived at the hotel at 8:00 a.m. we did not really expect that our room would be ready at that early hour. We were wrong! Not only was the room ready, but our corner-view room on the 48th floor had as spectacular a view as one could imagine. One wall of windows framed a breathtaking view of the Brooklyn Bridge, the Manhattan Bridge, and the East River. The other windows looked out toward the Statue of Liberty, and of course, over the site of the World Trade Center. The view of the WTC site was sobering but we were also struck by how resilient the city remains, not only by the expansive view, but by the overall vibrancy of the city.The hotel was very impressive, attractive, well-staffed and extremely well-priced by NYC standards. The room, with it's contemporary furnishings, comfortable size, nice plasma television, was a relaxing retreat after our days and evenings out on the town. The only drawback, and it was a minor one, was that the financial district is not well-stocked with good restaurants. However, Tribeca/Soho and the city beyond are only a short walk away, and buses/subways/cabs are at the hotel's doorstep.

<Author>drgnfly30
<Content>July 4th Holiday at the Millenium Hilton We stayed at the Millenium Hilton from July 3-6th.... Paid $229 with 2 free breakfast buffett coupons per day as a part of their BounceBack deal that I booked directly from their website. We took the path over from NJ to save on the $45 per night parking fee. The hotel couldn't have been more convenient to the Path station. We had a double room for me, husband  sons 15  10... , we were in room 2001 on the 20th floor facing Century 21  the WTC site, it was apparently one of the larger standard rooms.. WOW if these rooms are big for NYC I'd hate to see an average room! The 2 double beds appeared to be smaller than doubles I've slept on in the past..(we joked it's not a California King but a Manhattan Double!) Because they were so small we called for a roll away for DS10 - it was $25 for the entire stay. The TV was cool. The shower heads were small  I would have expected something a bit more posh for the hotel. No turn down service however the first night there were some chocolates sitting on the mini bar but nothing after that.The Stage Deli that was mentioned in other reviews was great! We ate their twice... if you want delivery late at night we found the only thing was Charleys - their Pizza was WAY too greasy. The breakfast buffett was perfect... since it was free as a part of our BounceBack rate... I'd never pay $18.95 Plus Tax for it!! The pool was nice, especially for the kids. While we weren't in the thick of NY, we appreciated the 'down' time  the subways were easily navigated with a small subway map we got from the NYC tourism site. We took a taxi back from the Circle Line (pier 83 or so?) for about $15. I'd definately consider staying here again for the right price...

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great deal and good service Stayed here in May with 4 of my girlfriends in a suite. There was a king size bed and separate living room with a sleep sofa. We got the suited for $299/night. Compared to some of the hotels in New York the space was right on time. The rooms were very clean but beware of the mini-bar. If you touch or remove anything it will be reflected on the bill. My girlfriend moved a beer to place a beverage in the refrigerator and promptly informed the front desk of the situation. An inventory of the items will be taken when you leave and any issues can be settled then. Did I mention the plasma TV to watch by the bed and the 32 in. in the separate living room area. The hotel is DIRECTLY across from Ground Zero/Subway and view was spectacular. Hard to imagine the chaos and horror of 9-11. How could I forget, Century 21 (discount name brand/designer) shopping store was practicully next door and the location is convenient for walking around and site seeing. Cabs and limos were not too bad for the cost. The bellhop (very cute) got us a limo to our Broadway play for $45/roundtrip. It is a short drive to Times Square and the sites there are unbelievable. Street vendors crowd the sidewalks on the weekend so be aware of your surrondings. I will definitely have to stay there again.

<Author>InAnIndianaTown
<Content>Catch Your Own Cab My husband and I stayed just one night at the Millenium Hilton. The front desk staff was wonderful; they even gave us a complimentary upgrade to a Junior Suite when my husband explained that he had flown my mom in as a birthday surprise to me, so she actually had a pull-out sofa to sleep on. The room was huge by NY standards and very clean. The air conditioning unit was loud, but we got used to it. Nice linens. Concierge was hit or miss - and understaffed. The persistant bellman tried to convince us to take a town car back to the airport and when we said no, he flagged down a cab for us, and the cab driver was sketchy and didn't have a medallion number. He charged us more than $20 over the going rate back to LaGuardia and refused to give us his medallion number when we threatened to report him. The sketchiest part of it all was that the bellman tipped the cabbie when we left the hotel. It was clear that the bellman was paying the unlicensed cabbie to take us on the scenic route to the airport. This hotel makes up in ambiance what it lacks in service. We'd stay there again, but call our own cabs! :)

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Best value stay in NYC My wife and I are both in our late 20's, live in London (although we're both New Zealanders) and have now stayed at the Millennium Hilton twice in the last year. We stayed for 8 nights last Sept for the US Open tennis and then for 6 nights in the first week of May for a shopping trip (to take advantage of a public holiday in the UK). Based on conversations with friends and work colleague, I don't think anywhere offers better value - PROVIDED you want to stay in a hotel of at least 3 stars. The best news is that the Hilton is a 4 to 5 star hotel with no inconsistencies in the rooms - and this was a prime consideration as we didn't want to have to deal with the disappointment of pictures on the websites not reflecting reality, I guess this is the benefit of staying at the Hilton. The rooms were very roomy for NY (on our first visit we had to stay a couple of nights at Club Quarters Downtown because of the Republican Convention so we can make the contrast), the bed was big and comfortable and the plasma screen topped it all off. We stayed in a standard room with views over Ground Zero both times, on the 17th and 23rd floors respectively 鈥?the rooms and experience were identical. Our nightly rate was USD200 and USD280 respectively (booked direct through (---) as their rates are cheapest) - for a hotel in NY that is not a lot and I personally think this is exceptional value as you'll pay a similar amount to stay at the Pennsylvania near Madison Square garden and I don't think the two hotels compare (check out the reviews and real pictures on this site). There is easy access to everywhere via the metro. Just beware that if you're coming from JFK, because the hotel is downtown then the advertised flat rate of USD45 does not apply because that only gets you to midtown - this is not helped by the fact that a lot of taxi drivers and private car drivers do not know the downtown roads very well. We never had breakfast there as a) it was expensive and b) we鈥檇 rather eat out of the hotel so I can鈥檛 comment on it鈥檚 quality, but if you want a nice NY breakfast then go to The Kitchenette on 80 W. Broadway at Warren St.

<Author>banana0711
<Content>Nice hotel and facilities We stayed in a parlor suite over the Memorial Day weekend for my daughter's 7th birthday. We were on the 53rd floor with a view over the World Trade Center site - would have liked a city view but the parlor suites don't have that view. The parlor suites are made out of 2 regular rooms with one room turned into a living room with a queen sleep sofa. They are nice since there is a full bath in each room - good for families or business travelers who need a meeting room and want to block off the bedroom. The bedroom had a king bed, desk and TV - nice but nothing super. The room was clean and service was good. The plasma TV is nice but nothing new anymore. Being a primarily business hotel, the TV lacked children's channels and there was no way to hook up a DVD player to it so our daughter could watch movies. The bed was fine but one night the sheets were a bit scratchy so it was hard to sleep.We had a good package that included valet parking (at $45/day a good deal if you drive) and we got free breakfast with my husband's gold hilton membership. They had a nice breakfast buffet, but quite expensive unless you plan to really eat a lot. If our breakfast had not been free, we would not have eaten there but the food was good and the selections plentiful. You can also order off the menu.The indoor pool on the 5th floor was very nice - the main reason we chose to stay there since our daughter loves to swim. The fitness facilities were also quite good for a hotel.Transportation was convenient but if you plan to rely on taxis and want to get to mid or up town, it can take a while. It is best to know your way around since the cab drivers were inconsistent and sometimes seemed to be trying to make money out of their trips.Overall, we had a really good experience and our daughter loved the various views from up high. We would stay there again.  
<Date>May 31, 2005

<Content>Great service, very proffessional Stayed here May 26 to 29 with my girlfriend. Had read lots of positive reviews. We weren't disapointed. Room was ready on arrival. Although we had asked for king size and got queen. Went to front desk and had room changed right away. Beautifull views of course. Away from all the action of uptown but only 12 minutes by subway, station is footsteps away. Not even 5 minutes to canal street, Little Italy and Chinatown..... You must visit Little Italy, its worth the trip. Starbucks coffee right around the corner and stage door deli 1 block away, serve amazing breakfest (try the 4 egg western omelet.wow).. The room was spacious, very modern and clean. Bathroom was amazing, lots of space, pressure and hot water.We checked in Thursday at around 7:00pm, checked out Sunday at 12:00 but were only charged 2 days of parking wich was cool cause at 45$/day, it gets expensive. A few minutes away from all the action A definite 4 star at a 2-3 star price...

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Millenium Hilton--great in every respect While we were anxious to go to NYC, after reading so many horror stories about hotels there, I was feeling a little stressed about finding an affordable, decent place to stay with our daughters and 4-year-old grandson. Since we were going over a long weekend (May 20-23, 2005), someone suggested the Financial District and so we booked ourselves at the Millenium Hilton at 55 Church Street, directly across from Ground Zero. It was wonderful in every respect. Super convenient to the subway--station was directly across the street and we were able to get to Central Park, Natural History Museum, Intrepid Museum and ferry to Statue of Liberty/Ellis Island without having to transfer subway lines. There are several places to get late night/early morning snacks (Starbucks, Burger King, deli, TGIFridays, Caruso's Pizza) within walking distance so you don't have to pay for hotel-rate food.The staff was very helpful, especially the concierge who let us check our luggage upon arrival and also the day we departed. We had a large room with two double beds and a rollaway which easily accomodated the five of us. We were on the 11th floor, overlooking Ground Zero. The room was very upscale, IMMACULATE, wide screen TV...all the amenities. Nice pool and fitness center on 5th floor which we also enjoyed. And the weekend rate was only $215/night as opposed to hotels in midtown Manhatten that raise their rates on Friday and Saturday. Highly, highly recommend for families who come on the weekend for its convenience, quality of service, exceptional value, and 4-star rooms. I can't think of one complaint!

<Author>BringHomeTroops
<Content>Good, modern hotel in convenient location Just got back from my second stay great at the Millenium Hilton. We got a corner room on a high floor with BEAUTIFUL views including the Statue of Liberty. The room was spacious (bigger than standard non-corner room), bathroom was wonderful - lots of counter space, and very comfy bed (and I'm picky). I love these rooms because they are in better shape than all of the other hotels I've stayed in. It was completely renovated in 2003 and has a modern decor, not that busy old-style colonial look with heavy fabrics, etc. Also, since rooms are almost all with one king bed, not many children stay there which keeps down on the wear and tear. While overall I really liked the place for the price (179.00), there were a few odd things. The sheets and towels we got in our room on the first night were wonderful. Luxurious soft and thick high thread count sheets, thick soft towels. However, on night two, they were changed out with ordinary low-thread count scratchy sheets, and towels were smaller and not as nice at all. We got turn-down service with chocolates 2 of the 3 nights. The third night no chocolates. I really could care less about turn-down service, in fact I think it's ridiculous - I can easily turn down my sheets - but a little inconsistent. The room was cleaner than average but not perfect - stain on comforter and on wall, a few hairs in shower. Room was ready on arrival and they held our luggage after we checked out until our train left town. Shower pressure was good with lots of hot water. Didn't use room service or eat at the hotel, too many great places in NY to eat there. We didn't mind the location at all. It is on top of several subway lines and a 20 min walk to the Village. I've stayed in the other Hilton in NYC and this one is far better for a lot less money. Hope this helps!  
<Date>May 25, 2005

<Author>jdcotr
<Content>Great hotel I couldn't fault this hotel. The room was clean, tidy and a reasonable size. There was an iron, hair dryer and a safe in the room but no coffee maker which is only a minor gripe. The 42 plasma screen was very nice and there were a wide variety of channels to choose from including the usual pay movies. There was also internet access through the TV and you can checkout using the TV's interactive features which was useful.Room service always arrived promptly and wasn't overpriced by hotel standards. The food was also very good. We only ate breakfast in the restaurant and this was mainly due to laziness rather than the food or service. You are far better going to one of the many Deli's along Broadway which serve a better variety of food and for a quarter of the cost. Beware if you take travellers cheques as they will only change $250 worth per stay. I would advise using ATM's instead of travellers cheques as there are hundreds nearby.The staff were all polite and they were happy to stow our bags after checkout as our flight wasn't until 20:00. Overall a very enjoyable stay and I wouldn't hesitate to go back.

<Author>rrrucke
<Content>Hilton Manager snubs my online hotel purchase My stay: 4/22 - 4/24/05. Two weeks ago, I purchased three hotel rooms on Priceline for $1,067 for a weekend in NYC. As a resident of NJ and NYC worker, I was extremely happy to have my bid accepted and it was also upgraded to a 4-star hotel, called the Millennium Hilton, located across the street from the WTC. On 4/22, I was checked into an unclean room. It appeared as if someone had used the room and then left in a hurry. Since this is not standard service of any hotel, I called the front desk to complain. After many apologies, the front desk offered me an upgrade to a jr suite but it required a little time to be cleaned. After 90 minutes of waiting in the bar and checking with the front desk on the room status, I was checked into a beautiful jr suite with a fantastic view. Unfortunately, the wireless phone near the bed didn't work so I was forced to use my cell phone along with another family's room. Anyway, the next morning, we left early for shopping. When we returned at noon, a few of us found stained pillows and our phone lines still didn't work. When I called the hotel on my cell phone to complain about the dirty sheets and bad phones, they apologized and sent someone up. Thankfully, the housekeeping mgr came by and apologized for the dirty laundry and he confiscated our pillows. He promised to have our sheets replaced then he offered to comp my family for dinner at the hotel. I was very surprised by the offer and I immediately told him there were 9 people in our party. To my further surprise, he said this number would be no problem. Then about 15 mins later, the front desk mgr called to apologize for the bad phones and explained that they would have to come up and move our beds to repair the wiring. Due to this inconvenience, the manager asked if we would mind moving to some other rooms but I refused the offer because we had already unpacked and had entirely too many shopping bags to contend with. The front desk mgr then offered to comp my room for the valet parking which is $45/day/car and we had 2 cars. Of course I also jumped on this offer and thanked her. Later that night, we all headed to the bar before dinner. While in the bar, I went to check with the front desk to see about our dinner compensation. The clerk promised to check on this and find me in the bar (which was less than 35 feet away). After the standard 90 min wait of checking back and forth, the night manager came to the bar to explain that my hungry party of nine was not going to receive the dinner compensation as promised. Of course, I pitched a small fit during our private conversation. I explained that we were all counting on this promise, especially since a great portion of our day was used to discuss how thoughtful we thought the Hilton was after all the many problems. Unfortunately, the night manager had the nerve to tell me that the Hilton was not trying to pay for our entire stay considering we didn't pay that much for our rooms online. I thought his condescending tone coupled with this statement was in extremely bad taste and very unprofessional. I quickly figured out that he was trying imply that we were trying to scam the hotel when this was not the case. I told him that we were only asking for what we were promised and nothing more. We ended the conversation so he could call the daytime front desk mgr at home. When he returned, he explained in a nasty tone that the daytime front desk mgr was unaware of the dinner comp and she thought the only comp offer was the valet. I told the night manager that it was obvious that their managers had a communication problem and as their customer I didn't appreciate being caught in the middle. Since the conversation was going no where, I demanded their names and the contact names for the General Manager, CEO and the Customer Service Complaint line. I told him I planned to complain. When he returned with the information, he still had a condescending tone in front of my family which was really quite shocking since we were in a 4-star hotel. In all my travels, I have never been made to feel like my money was less than valuable because I used the internet to make the purchase. It's obvious the Hilton's philosophy is that online customers are second class citizens!! Based on my experience, I suggest you patron a different hotel chain. Thanks for listening.

<Author>ctmarcus
<Content>Some good suggestions... The millenium hilton really is a fantastic hotel! We stayed for 3 nights in January and I thought the reviews on this site were quite accurate. The rooms are small, but I hear that is the norm in New York. We had a view of the reconstruction of Ground Zero - I thought it was amazing. However, if this is something that may bother you, you need to request a room on the other side of the building because you are literally right over the site. There is also very easy access to all subway lines and we took the subway all over the city. Be sure and visit Century 21, the discount department store right across the street. I also highly recommend the Stage Door Deli just accross the street for the best sandwitches in the area. We ate there 3 times in 4 days - the portions are huge and prices reasonable. The best meal I have ever had in my life was at Raouls in SOHO - a short cab ride from the millenium hilton (be sure and make a reservation because the host is quite rude - but it is worth it). It is fantastic and not terribly expensive. A friend who is a local recommended it to us and I assure you it will not disappoint!!

<Author>Ge0ff
<Content>Highly Recommended Hotel Chose the Millenium hilton after reading trip advisor review and was not disappointed. Sleek hotel with large rooms and excellent views. friends were at the same time staying in the Roosevelt and their rooms were very small in comparison. Staff always willing to help, breakfast in the hotel was the usual hotel standard ie good. also ate breakfast in local eatery just along the road which was also good and of course a lot cheaper, but you do get views from the restaurant over ground zero and it is a lot more convenient to eat initially in the hotel. Taxis are plentiful and the subway is on the doorstep taking only 10mins or so to get you uptown. You can walk to Battery Park to catch the ferry to The Statue of Lberty. You actually see more of New York staying in Lower Manhatten if you take the cabs uptown, than if you have a central hotel which you just tend to walk out of and wander locally. We did the tour of Manhatten in the bus on the last day of our trip and realised that we had already seen most locations when using the cabs to  from the hotel. I found myself giving directions to other folk after only a day or two in new York! If you are looking for a hotel that has a 'happenning' bar/lounge then look elswhere but if you want a clean, efficient hotel with large rooms/bathroom and those plasma TVs with great views and ease of access to Manhatten then I would thoroughly recommend this hotel. If I was returning to New York I would go back to the Millenium tomorrow

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great stay Stayed at the Millenium for 6 nights March/April 2005 to celebrate wedding anniversary. Used Tripadvisor to help select hotel and reviews helped us to choose. We were able to gain access to our room without any problems as soon as we checked in at midday. Hotel staff were friendly and helpful. Advice from the Concierge made for a successful trip. Our room was clean and well appointed-our tv at home seems very small! Views at night with twinkling lights were lovely but obviously one needs to be aware of the hotel location. The church next door has a moving exhibition for 9/11 events.Although the hotel is downtown Manhattan this is still convenient for Statue of Liberty and Ellis Island, Battery Park (bus tour) and downtown heliport all within 10 minutes walk. Subway was opposite and a NY yellow cab uptown averaged $10-12.Hotel restaurant was ok and you were able to fill up on the buffet breakfast. Starbucks around the corner from Century 21 was a good alternative. Various restaurants on the ground floor of the Financial Centres opposite were useful for quiet evening meals-good walks along the River Hudson too.A busy but enjoyable holiday. I will have a lasting memory of swimming in the hotel pool at 5.30am-adjusting to time difference on first morning! watching the sunrise over the Manhattan buildings, unmistakeably New York!

<Author>Miro586
<Content>Modern Hotel with great views I give this hotel four and a half stars. It is very much as described on the tin. It is a large modern skyscraper hotel. Its USP is the terrific views from the higher floors. My room on the 50th floor on the North West corner had a wonderful view uptown including both the Hudson and East river. Apart from the view, the rooms are spacious, well furnished and with good bathrooms. The beds are very comfortable. The plasma TV can be used to access the internet (for $10 per day). The staff are efficient and very helpful. The hotel is close to subway stations for five of the North-South subway lines, so it is easy to get to points uptown.My only reservation is food. The quality is entirely adequate but it is not outstanding. It is also not cheap.I paid a rate of $242 ($212 plus tax). In my experience this is good value for this level of hotel. I would certainly use the Millenium Hilton again.

<Author>atcken
<Content>Hilton in Lower Manhattan My wife and I have stayed at this hotel twice. The first time was over the Thanksgiving holiday '04 and the 2nd time was last weekend (Mar '05). Over Thanksgiving we didn't want to stay near Times Square and all the parade crowds so we decided to try this lower Manhattan Hilton property. The hotel has been fairly recently renovated as it sits directly across the street from the WTC site. In fact for both our stays, our room view looked down into the WTC site and across towards the Hudson. Awesome, incredible view but be aware that it might be disturbing for some to know they are looking directly at the at the site of the horrific WTC tragedy. The views on the other side of the hotel are just as good as you look over the city and out at the Brooklyn Bridge and East River.The rooms are nice but not lavish. The king beds are firm but comfortable enough. The bathrooms are average size with a tub/shower combo. Rooms overall are average hotel size with a reading chair and desk. There is internet access for a fee in the rooms however the lounge in the lobby has free wireless access. A nice touch in each of the rooms is a 42 plasma TV! Church and Dey restaurant on the 3rd floor is a decent American restaurant. And the Liquid Assets lounge in the lobby is good but the drinks are expensive (ex. $9 glass of wine). Highlights of this hotel for me have been the very nice indoor pool on the 5th floor (and a nice fitness room). And the location has worked out well, expecially if you fly into EWR. The PATH trains are now working directly from Newark Penn station so you can train from the airport to Newark Penn and then take the PATH train directly to WTC, which is across the street from the Millenium Hilton. Cost for this trip via trains is $8.30 - quite a bargain for traveling from an airport to a hotel in Manhattan. Of course subway stops are nearby and it is a short walk from the hotel to South Street Seaport.If you don't mind riding the subway or other trains around and to Manhattan, (or you can just take taxis of course) this is a great hotel ranging in price with specials from $175 to $225 per night.  
<Date>Mar 17, 2005

<Author>JessieWillow
<Content>Fantastic! Having read the reviews on this hotel, I was worried that my expectations would be too high but luckily I wasn't disappointed! My husband and I spent 3 nights here from 3rd to 6th March 2005 and found the hotel to be superb in every way. We were originally given a room on the 15th floor but after we spoke to the reception staff about getting a room on a higher floor, we were given one on the 52nd floor! The views day and night were amazing especially as the weather was very clear and fine. The location is great. After my last trip to New York, when I stayed in a grubby hotel in Midtown, I was keen to experience a different area. So many interesting places are walking distance away, such as Chinatown, Little Italy, South Street Seaport and Greenwich Village. Even when we occasionally ventured uptown, the subway station was right outside.The room was immaculate and very clean although it did get quite warm at night. One evening I opened the little window and couldn't shut it again but a member of staff arrived in minutes to assist us! In all, the staff were very helpful, especially the bellboys who always had a smile on their faces! I would DEFINITELY stay here again, particularly when compared to the over-priced dives in Midtown.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Perfect Hotel! Have just returned from a 3 night stay at the millenium Hilton, and I have to say I would recommend it to anyone. Staff were freindly and helpful, the standard of the room was very good (42 plasma screen, say no more !), clean with nice bathroom and one of the most comfortable beds I have ever slept in. There's a nice bar/restaurant on the third floor that we often called in for a couple of drinks to watch the sun go down, and prices were ok as well. I noticed some reviewers had a downer on the restaurant, but hey you are in New York, if you are going to complain about hotel breakfast/food prices etc. then you should really be out getting some real NY food! There are loads of diners etc. nearby which are just the job. Location is good, the subway is literally right outside of the main entrance and you are in easy walking distance of Soho / Battery Park / South Street Seaport and various others. If you don't mind walking past the twin towers memorial every day (and all the toursists grinning and posing for photos in front of it - missing the point totally!!???) it's pretty good overall. The bell staff had no problem looking after our bags, as we checked out at 12.00 but didn't fly until 8pm, so we had another full day in NY without worrying about our bags. When I come back to NY, I will definately stay here again !.

<Author>travelismymiddename
<Content>Would stay again We stayed at this property Feb 18-20th in rm 3410. It was my husband's birthday so we requested a high floor with a nice view. The room overlooked ground zero and was a decent size for NY standards. There wasn't anything special about the decor, but it was nice and the room was very clean upon arrival. I wrote to the Hilton upon my return and they have been extremely responsive regarding my complaint. Also, the turn down service was just that, turn down of the bed only. We have stayed at many hotels in NYC and their turn down service also included a tidy-up of the bath and room. Other than that I enjoyed the hotel and loved the fact that Century 21 is across the street. I would stay here again but would choose someplace else for a special occasion like a birthday or anniversary.

<Author>dp_visser
<Content>Don't overlook or underestimate this hotel! My partner and I just returned from a 3-night stay at the Millenium Hilton. Although a bit apprehensive at first about the location, we were more than happy here. Just about every subway line stopped either in front of or near the hotel (within one block), which meant that Up- and Downtown were just minutes away. We treated ourselved to a junior suite, which was nice as we had a corner overlooking Ground Zero on one side and the Empire State Building on the other! Unfortunately we did not get a room on a very high floor as we arrived a bit late on a holiday weekend in the US, but nonetheless the personnel did their best to accomodate our wishes. Very helpful and friendly, even at 2:00 am when you can't get into your room!!!Only downfall is that the rooms are not completely soundproof, so you will hear the jackhammers at or around Ground Zero. The construction there goes on 24 hrs a day, 365 days a year, so no getting around it! But then again, if you are tired enough you will sleep!As for breakfast, the hotel has its standard buffet breakfast, which we did not go for as down the road to the left of the hotel (next to the Brooks Brothers building) you have a small diner called Panini  Co., where you can have a full breakfast for $ 3 to $ 4. Pretty much all the people we ran into there were from the hotel! Also, if you just want a good cup of coffee, there is a Starbucks next to the hotel plus a baguette shoppe (not all too cheap, but cheaper than the Hilton)! And if you go to Broadway (parallel to Church Street and behind the hotel, you have a myriad of restaurants: TGI Fridays, McDonald's, etc. And all are cheaper than their counterparts in and around Times Square!All-in-all a great stay and we will be going back!  
<Date>Feb 23, 2005

<Author>excentrus
<Content>Very modern and very cool What a great hotel! A fifty-five story, sleek black 4 star marvel. The absolute best weekend deal in NYC. Go directly to the Hilton website for information on super weekend web-rates. All the employees were friendly and helpful. Check in was really quick....and it was up to the 23rd floor. The MOST comfortable king size bed possible and a 42 inch plasma TV were waiting. I didn't realize it was Martin Luther King weekend (I'm Canadian)....and there were LOTS of tourists. I loved being downtown...away from the crowds. NYC is a fabulous place but there can be too much frenetic energy, and I liked retreating to lower Manhattan. It was very peaceful. All sorts of subway lines are located within a one block radius of the hotel entrance....so NYC is at your doorstep. I think that this hotel is geared towards the business traveller and the prices probably rise dramatically during the week. One word of caution : If a bird's eye view of Ground Zero will bother you...you might want to pass on this one.

<Author>u761154
<Content>Great Xmas Stay Stayed on Dec 26th for 3 nights, they checked us in early which was a bonus. Booked the city view room directly overlooking Ground Zero, for $150 per night from the Hilton website.Room was clean and a good size, especially for NY hotels. 42 plasma tv screen was great and the Hilton Heavenly Bed is the most comfortable at any hotel I have stayed at.Very quiet room and ideal for getting away from the busy streets further uptown. Century 21 is right next door for those who are looking for shopping bargains.We had breakfast once at the restaurant, had good choice in the hot and cold buffet, which cost $16 each. However, on the other days we went to the numerous cheap delis and cafes around the hotel, you'll never be short of choice.The tube stops are right on the doorstep, and is only a 10-15 min metro ride to Times Square, very convenient, and only costs $2 for a single trip. Taxi from airport is $45 flat fee (metered in other direction), but suggest you get the metro from/to Howard's Beach ($2) and the AirTran ($5), takes about about 40 mins.Would agree with some of the other reviews that not all the staff are friendly, however would highly recommend this hotel and would stay here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>A very good hotel Stayed in this hotel for our first visit to New York from 26th November until 1st December after having read the reviews posted on this site.We had a room on the 24th Floor overlooking Ground Zero, check-in was hassel free and we were in the room before 3pm, the bed was indeed very comfortable and the plasma screen tv big, my only complaints with the room are that you could hear toilets and showers being used in the other rooms, and the chairs were not very comfortable.We had breakfast the first morning in the hotel restaurant and I would not advise anyone to do this as there are many cheaper places around the hotel ($46 for two buffet-breakfasts), such as Andrews coffee shop on pearl and john street.The staff were very helpful with the exception of the concierge who on a number of occasions got into the lift before us whilst we were waiting and did not ask which floor we would like.Whilst I agree with other reviewers that this is an excellent hotel I wouldn't reccomend it, as it really is out of the way and whilst there is a subway station opposite, the system is not very outsider friendly, such as knowing the direction of the train or the next stop indeed if the train even makes a stop at your required station as the notices advising of the stops are small if non existent.Nonetheless anyone spending a few days in New York would not be dissappointed with this hotel.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great hotel! Just returned today from a 2 night stay at the Millenium Hilton and had a great time. The room was clean and large and we had a wonderful view of the Statue of Liberty from our window. The hotel is directly across the street from Ground Zero which is quite a place to see and remember. If this bothers you you probably should make sure before you check in that your room isn't in the front of the hotel. The staff couldn't have been nicer and more helpful. The subway station is right across the street and will take you uptown to Times Square,Rockefeller Center,etc.,but make sure that you know exactly which stop you need to get off at or you could get lost easily if you don't live in Manhattan. It may be hard to use the subway if you have very young children(we were with 9 and 12 year olds that complained alot about it!). There is a great deli,Starbucks,and a Dunkin Donuts all within easy walking distance from the hotel which is really nice. We also walked to Battery Park and took the ferry to the Statue of Liberty and Ellis Island. We thought the location was a nice retreat for us after long days of walking around in the city and we had no problems with noise at all. If you can get a good rate,this is a great place to stay while visiting NY and I'd give it an A!  
<Date>Nov 8, 2004

<Author>Goldrusswoman
<Content>Overall great, but Overwhelmed staff For my first time in Manhattan, we chose one night at the Millenium Hilton. The room was modern, clean, and roomy (I was concerned given reviews about small hotel rooms in NYC). Bathroom was large, bright, and very clean. We had made reservations for a king bed (the only thing available on the Hilton reservation site), but they let us change to 2 double beds at check in (no extra charge). We had a partial view of Ground Zero. The room was very quiet during the night despite the fact that the hotel was either at or near capacity.When we checked in at 9 AM, we left our bags---the front desk was very quiet and the person behind the desk very helpful. When I returned at 4 PM to actually pick up my keys, it was a different story---with 6 people behind the desk they seemed really overwhelmed and there was a line that seemed to last longer than it should have. Getting someone to help with my bags up to the room seemed impossible, so I took my own stuff up, which was OK, except for the fact that when I got to the room, neither of the two keys that they gave me worked. Called down with the phone in the hall and a security person came right up, confirmed my ID, and gave me a key that did work. I have never had this happen in all my personal and business travel, and I can only attribute it to the overwhelmed front desk.We did not eat at the hotel, but had breakfast at the Stage Door Deli right next door---it was fabulous. There is a Starbucks around the corner too.Besides the front desk, the only thing not so great about this hotel is the location. As my first time to Manhattan, I had no idea as to distances, where things are, etc. Next time I would stay closer to Central Park and the shopping district. Although it was raining when we left, the hotel staff were able to get us a car immediately to the airport at a reasonable price.Despite the check-in issues, I would stay here again if I needed to be downtown.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Expensive, but worth it!!!! Arrived in NY at 6:30am, check-in wasn't until 3pm, but the front desk was kind enough to let us check in our bags and call us on our cell phones as soon as an available room was ready. The people there were really helpfull, kind and considerate. Even the bell guys helped us find places to go for the meantime until check in.We finally got a call an hour and a half before 3pm, which they gave us the choice on the 21st or 12th floors. The room was kinda small but more than enough room for 2 people. It had an amazing 48 flat screen TV, marble bathroom counter, an executive desk, and views over the late WTC and Hudson River from a far.As stated in most of the other reviews, Ground Zero was across the street of the hotel, Century 21 shopping was on one side, while the oldest church in NY was on the other. During the day, the streets are jam packed with people going to work, or visitors paying their respects to Ground Zero, at night... empty. It was so convenient to have the subway just a couple steps from the hotel to bring you wherever you wanted to go in the city, plus taxi comming around every second to look for passengers. If you got the legs and pretty fit to walk a long distance, you can always walk 5-10 min north to Canal St, Chinatown, shops in broadway, and SoHo's. Another 5-10 min south to battery park to catch a cruise ship to see the statue.Overall, the stay was wonderfull. Ive visited NY 7 times with friends but usually staying close to busy Time Square where most of the other places were equal to run down roach hotels that need renovations. Millenium is the perfect place to stay with your significant other, where its busy during the day, slow and relaxing at night, and convenient for any method of public transportation.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Great Views/Great Stay We stayed at the Millenium Hilton from 30th Sept to 3 Oct for a joint birthday/anniversary do' and we loved it! Our king corner room was on the 53rd floor and we had such fabulous city views, I found myself waking up in the wee hours of the morning just to see the spectacular sunrises. Watching the sleepy city come to life was one of the high points of our trip. The evening views were wonderful as well, with the buildings all sophisticated shimmer. Probably to the shock of a few dedicated office workers, we slept with the curtains wide open, just to revel in the wonderful glittery magic.I often use Trip Advisor and I'm pleased the reviews were spot on. We stayed at the Regency on Park Avenue earlier on our trip and did not like it at all! Overpriced, snooty and the room was dull in comparison.I would have liked a coffee pot, but we had a Starbucks right around the corner. It really is taking over the world! The room was very clean, room service efficient and we enjoyed the plasma television. My husband had a hard time saying his goodbyes.I agree with other reviewers that ground zero was a sobering experience. I was a bit apprehensive before we visited as I wasn't sure what to expect - but people paying their respects seem to bear this in mind and it makes it a lot less of a circus affair and more of a quiet, respectful memorial. Still difficult to take in though...The staff at the hotel were cheerful and helpful. We read about the electronic fridges so didn't even attempt to open it to gaze at the forbidden goodies. There is a giftstore downstairs with (still) expensive and limited snacks, but a lot cheaper than the minibar. Around the corner from the hotel you will find a few shops that sell ciggies, beverages and sweets - stockup for midnight munchies. The hotel has icebuckets and ice for your sodas. We had breakfast only once in the hotel and found it expensive and so-so. There is a Stage deli near the church half a block away, or wander around until you hit a diner type serving breakfast.The area is very rushed during weekdays (especially lunch!) with all the workers milling around. The weekend can be a little bit of a let down with some restaurants only catering to the Mon-Fri crowd, but this is an excellent time to get some shopping done or visit some of the other places on your list like Chinatown.Speaking of shopping - Century 21 is right next door - Their motto is 'New York's best kept secret', but we joked that the secret was out because EVERYONE seems to know about it. We foolishly attempted to shop on Friday at 5:30 PM - we could barely walk through the store. We returned on Sunday afternoon and it was slightly less crowded. South Seaport is a short walk away - a nice surprise and a twist on the usual mall scene with good seafood to be had. It is relaxing just to walk around and look at the boats and water with benches for you to gaze and take in the tranquility. Greenwich, Soho etc/ all a subway away for more trendy shopping - and Times Square is dead easy to get to for more hectic fun. From our hotel window we could see the Statue of Liberty and the fabulous Brooklyn Bridge. We enjoyed Ellis island and the boat ride provided some good photo opportunities.Overall we really enjoyed our stay and will be staying here again.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Will definitely return! We booked our Sept. 21-24 stay in NYC at the Millenium Hilton based on reviews we read on Trip Advisor. We were not disappointed. The location is fantastic. Our room was not ready when we attempted to check in but then it was only 11 a.m. They upgraded us to a Junior Suite on the 23rd floor overlooking Ground Zero. Besides the remarkably clean room, we fell in love with the Plasma TV. We found ourselves returning to our room early just to lie in bed, sip wine and watch the big screen TV. The staff was the best from check in until check out. Friendly, courteous and efficient. I especially loved the nightly turn down service with bottled water and chocolates each evening. I used to be a hotel maid so I tend to be a harsh judge of cleanliness in hotel rooms. Our room was spotlessly clean each day and I commend the housekeeping staff. We had only one problem when we were charged for the mini bar when we did not use it. I understood though because each item has an electronic eye under it which we set off when we removed some items to look at them. The front desk happily took our word for it when we called and took the charge off the bill with no questions asked. We are Diamond Level Hilton Honors members who will continue to stay at Hampton Inns worldwide because we feel they work very hard to retain their customers.

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Gave away our room! Booked room through priceline for a weekend of sightseeing and shopping with family from out of town. The rates were reasonable, around $175.00/ night (non-holiday weekend), but was dissappointed to find that they do not have any double occupancy rooms. We were forced to reserve 3 rooms to accomodate everyone. The rooms are decently-sized and clean. Each room has a large flat screen tv and a king sized bed. The location is excellent, very close to canal street (Chinatown, Little Italy) and directly across the street from the World Trade Center/ Ground Zero. We had a dead on view of what used to be a modern marvel; 2 110-story office buildings which were cities within themselves. I spent a lot of time staring out the window reflecting on 9-11, it was a humbling experience.Ok, here are my biggest gripes with this hotel:1) There is NO lobby, and the small foyer in which you check in and out is so crowded and you will be waiting a while so I would suggest you stay somewhere else if you are at all claustrophobic. Also, this means there is no where to sit and relax or hang out. 2) The breakfast buffet. The bill was over $80 for 4 of us to eat at the buffet at the hotel's restaurant Church  Dey. The buffet was small, poorly stocked and WAY over-priced. There was hardly any food left when we ate at 10:00 a.m. on Sunday.3) The parking staff is hurrendous. We called ahead as they advised us to in order to avoid a wait. We packed and made our way down to the garage 45 minutes later to get our car only to wait another 45 minutes. No one would even look at us or ask us if we were being helped and finally after 25 minutes the attendant asked for our voucher. It was only then that he told us we had to have the voucher validated at the front desk first. We had to go back to the front desk and wait on the long line of guests checking out to get the stamp. Mind you, we had already waited on the line to check out, so I was very irritated to have to do it again. The parking staff was rude and unapologetic.5) Examine your final bill carefully, they charged us for items in the minibar that were not taken. Seems they will charge you if you move an item to a different spot in the fridge even if it's unopened.6) Last but not least, we had reserved 3 rooms, however the third room would not be occupied until the second night. We realized this glitch in our schedule too late to change our reservations so we decided to check all 3 rooms in upon arrival and leave the 3rd empty for the 1st night. We asked them to hold the keys at the front desk for our 3rd party until their arrival. All 3 rooms were to be adjacent to eachother on the same floor. When it came time for our 3rd party to get their key, the front desk informed us that they had given the room away. The room we had ALREADY PAID FOR! Turns out they, LUCKILY, had ONE room unoccupied that night due to an early check-out. We had no other choice, so we took the room which was on another floor. The front desk staff handled this situation terribly. They never apologized or seemed to realize what an inconvenience they had caused us. Had there been no more rooms in the hotel, what would we have done? PLUS this room was already paid for AND checked in! How could they have given it away? Bottom line, I wouldn't stay there again. Got a room at the Waldorf for $200 on Priceline for a holiday weekend and it was well worth the extra $25!!!

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Awsome views We stayed Fri and Sat nights on a 45th floor room. The hotel is across the street from the WTC site, so we had a lot to think about. Aside from ground zero, we had beautiful views of the city and the Hudson, and could even see mountains/hills in the distance. We got a deeply discounted rate by paying in advance (non-refundable).The hotel is across from the PATH train station to New Jersey, so this is a great location if you are coming in from Newark Airport. There are subway stations all over the place, so you can go anywhere from here, but be advised that the downtown area itself is pretty dead on the weekends. Many restaurants actually close up Sat and Sun, but you can take the subway to where you want. Chinatown is a moderate walk. For discounted theater tickets, the TKTS booth is nearby. (They have another booth in the Times Square area, but it has longer lines.) Of course, you can also walk down Wall St. or take a boat over to the Statue of Liberty, and I really enjoyed the South Street Seaport.The rooms are very nicely furnished, although a bit smallish. The plasma screen TVs are obscene overkill - who is going to sit around watching TV in NYC? The staff was courteous and helpful. I was disappointed that there wasn't a coffee machine in the room - I've gotten used to that as standard feature. There is coffee off the lobby for $1.75+ a cup. The way my wife guzzles, this can get a bit pricy.Oh yeah, don't touch anything in the mini-bar. It's computerized, so when I took something out to put my own soda in the fridge, it automatically registed as a change of $4.85 per soda. (Do some people really get that thirsty??) I had $30 of charges on my bill. They were nice about it and took them off, but it did take about 20 extra minutes at check out. I learned that this is not a fridge, it's a booby trap.Aside from that gripe, everything was great.  
<Date>Oct 1, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Anniversary weekend with a fractured foot We spent our 39th anniversary weekend at the Millenium Hilton. A week prior, I had fallen and fracured the bottom of my left foot. All our plans had been made and I hoped that being in a wheelchair would not ruin everything. From the moment we left our car, the weekend was perfect. The staff were wonderful and couldn't do enough to accomadate us. Our room was lovely. It was a corner room with a beautiful view both during the day and at night. The housekeeper on the 49th floor was so helpful and kind that it was almost like visiting with an old friend. The first night, we had reservations at Delmonico's, but enjoyed the brunch and dinner the second day. Brunch was well prepared, but not extensive, however the service was excellent and friendly. At dinner, the food was excellent and the wine list is comprehensive. Again, the service was warm and impressive. Every staff member from the dining room manager to the waiters was helpful, yet not intrusive. They escourted us to the elevators and made certain my wheelchair was in place before closing the doors. It was only a short two days, but we felt as though it had been much longer, it was such a lovely respite. We plan to return soon, but not wait for a special occasion.

<Author>jad376
<Content>Once again, spectacular. This hotel is one of my favorites in New York! I rate it above the Ritz-Carlton, W hotels, Tribeca Grand, and other 4- and 5-stars I've frequented. Our most recent stay was on a whim at the end of June; we were going into the city to see one of the Fahrenheit premieres, and decided to stay over because we love New York so much. Our cityview king room on the 51st floor had a breathtaking view of the Hudson River, ground zero, and to the north, the West Village and the Midtown skyline. When you reserve, make sure to request a room above the 45th floor. You will be above it all - especially if you stay before they construct the new world trade center. I sincerely recommend the King Corner rooms - when they're available, they're my favorite hotel rooms in New York, save for, maybe, the suites at The Donald's place... :) The bed was awesome...not quite a Heavenly Bed, but we slept wonderfully. The best features of the room always are the huge plasma screen TV with web access, and the big, comfy ergonomic leather chair at the desk. Room service was surprisingly good for the Hilton, but if you must eat their food, go downstairs to the Church  Dey dining room and have a proper dinner. For breakfast, there's a starbucks right next door and around the corner on Dey street. This hotel is convenient to the Tribeca/Soho party scene; the Tribeca Grand hotel is directly up Church st.. We enjoyed being in close proximity to the World Financial Center shops and the very cool Irish Hunger Memorial (located on the river across the street from ground zero), which we were able to see from our room. Now, about the staff. I've read people's complaints about rude or short employees that did not come off as overtly friendly...well...the truth of the matter is, the Millenium Hilton is a very large hotel, and the staff does seem rather stressed at times. However, if you take it all with a grain of salt and don't expect to be treated like absolute royalty (that's what $500/night places uptown are expected to be for), you will see that they're just simple hard working folks in the hotel business who are trying to run a first class operation. Oh - I almost forgot. The health club and indoor pool are fantastic, especially very early in the morning when they're empty. They also have a business center where you can print documents from the internet. If you can score a rate of under $199 per night, you'll love this hotel even more. Hilton, keep up the good work!  
<Date>Jul 24, 2004

<Author>A TripAdvisor Member
<Content>Good value for money Had 3 nights here in early July. I booked through Hilton's website and got a very good rate. Check in was easy and bags were delivered to the room within 5-10 minutes. Room overlooked WTC site and thanks to pretty good weather, the views were great. Overall the room was clean and modern looking. The big plasma screen TV made it easy to watch TV. There are lots of places in the neighborhood for both food and shopping, so if you have no pressing needs to be in Midtown, your stay here should be satisfactory at the very least. All employees were friendly and helpful.

<Author>catmint
<Content>Couldn't be better! We chose the Millenium Hilton after having seen it from the outside on a previous visit to New York - it is in our favourite part of the city and the sleek black tower looked impressive. As we were going back for our New York wedding and honeymoon we wanted everything to be just right. I was worried by some of the previous reviews which I had read before I left for New York. Well, I returned from New York yesterday and can honestly say that our stay in the Millenium Hilton was perfect. Other people have reported check in problems. We arrived early (2.10) and they checked us right in without a problem. The girl on the desk was efficient and when I asked if we could have a high floor for the view she allocated us a room on floor 52 which was a dream come true as this hotel has some of the best views in town. The bellhop was friendly and also efficient, escorting us to our room with our luggage. The elevators are amazingly quick and each floor only has eleven rooms (or thereabouts) which reduces noise and traffic in the corridors and means you don't have far to go to reach the elevator. The area outside the elevators on each floor is carpeted, so no footsteps while you are trying to sleep, and has a huge window with views to the rear of the hotel (i.e. the other side to the view from your room) - including the Brooklyn Bridge and the Woolworth building, and City Hall. Whatever floor you are on, you can travel to a high floor to see this. The room is a fair size for a New York room, with a wonderfully comfortable bed, tasteful furnishings and of course that plasma TV. You also get a desk with a reclining leather chair, and comfortable fabric covered chair, a small drinks table (plus glasses and an ice bucket of course), and more storage space than is usual in city hotels. Monday to Friday you get a newspaper at your door. The safe is easy to use and a handy feature. The bathroom is the best hotel bathroom I have seen, spacious and spotless. In fact everything is perfectly clean, and housekeeping are very thorough when they visit each day and also polite and friendly if you happen to meet them. Towels and bedlinen are all spotless and look new. The Neutrogena toiletries are a welcome touch and these are replenished if you use them so there is more than enough for your stay. And I haven't even told you about the best bit yet - the view! Yes, it is dominated by the World Trade Centre crater, but the work there now is preparing for rebuilding rather than tearing down (though one building remains to be dismantled). The World Financial Centre is opposite, and the Hudson river beyond where you can see some spectacular sunsets. Words can't do justice to the sight you see each time you draw back the curtains on the floor to ceiling windows but for us it was the highlight of our stay in New York. Each time we returned to our room it was a pleasure to be in this clean, comfortable, cool haven after the busy city streets, and to relax by the window and watch the hustle and bustle below was the best bit of all. The only thing that didn't work was the Interactive check out through the TV but we had nothing to pay on our account (no rogue charges at all, thankfully) and it took only a couple of seconds at the desk to check out. Our luggage was stored free of charge for us to collect later in the day, which took only minutes though they told us to allow 15min.I know where we'll be staying next time we return to New York City... in fact I wonder if they have rooms free for our first wedding anniversary?!  
<Date>Jun 29, 2004

<Author>Gslade
<Content>Just Average This was my first time back to the Millenium Hilton since September 11 had forced its closure. I had stayed in the hotel 4 or more times previous to 2001 and had always been a huge fan of the place- it was sleek, contemporary and well run. This time however, I wasn't as happy. Don't get me wrong- it's not awful, but the service was lacklustre in several areas and the place just seemed less luxurious- certainly it is not in my opnion a 4 star-more like a 3 star.Like other reviewers we encountered problems upon arrival with regards to the room booked. We had booked a Deluxe double on 33-55th floor with city view and on previous visits this had meant a corner room with a view uptown. The view we had was directly over Ground Zero. I don't particularly have a problem with that but certainly I would not call it a city view- unless they are referring to a New jersey city view. To be honest I couldnt be bothered to argue further with the clerk but as per other reviews- don't expect to necessarily get what you have booked! The check in staff were bordering on the surly and they even stated that breakfast wasnt included in the rate which I immediately corrected them on. We were told the breakfast vouchers would be sent to our room later that day and after 2 further inquiries and telephone calls- they were- hardly 4 star service huh?One further problem with the room is that we were on a non smoking floor. On our return to our room on the Saturday we could smell a strong cigarette smell in our room- which had a connecting door to teh room next door- we could smell teh smoke seeping through- and as non smokers it wasn't pleasant particularly as the hotel has very small windows that dont clear the air and air conditioning doesnt really help with smoke. We called the front desk who seemed totally disinterested and it was only when i got angry that he sent us housekeeping with an air purifier which took up a large chunk of our bedroom floorspace and wasnt that efficient- they seemed unconcerned that other guests were smoking on a non smoking floor which I think is unacceptable. Again they seemed disinterested and I was made to feel as if I was making a fuss!Housekeeping werent very efficient either- granted they tidied the room but it still looked messy- ie they didnt put away teh ironing board and the extra pillows and blankets were just left folded on the bed so the overall impression was a bit tatty.Now the good bits- the swimming pool is fab and the staff there are friendly and cheerful. Breakfast is good if you can get it as part of your room rate but overpriced otherwise. Room service is overpriced in my view and dont touch the minibar- $4.50 for a can of coke-! there are loads of delis nearby where we stocked up on beverages and stuffed them in our ice bucket to chill- much better!The rooms themselves may have been refurbished but the carpets look cheap and the place just seems more like a holiday inn than a premium Hilton property. The plasma screen TVs are Ok but they take the place of large mirrors that used to be wall mounted. Now the only mirrors are in the bathroom and on the bathroom door in a dark spot in the room. The bar in the lobby is quite nice but expensive- $12.50 for a cocktail seems a bit cheeky when it is really only a standard lobby bar.We stayed at Embassy Suites which is across from the Millenium by the Financial Center and this is a much better option if you can get a good rate.

<Author>Tifftoff
<Content>Great view, location, sights and more... I've been to New York before but stayed in the Times Square area. A lot of hustle and bustle but it was fun. This time I wanted to try a different area of New York, this is why I chose the Millenium Hilton. It's right across the street from Ground Zero, next door to Century 21 (great discount shopping), and about a ten minute walk to Battery Park which is where you grab the ferry to Ellis Island and Statue of Liberty, but there is much more to see at the Park than one would think. Just make sure you check to see if anything is going on at the Park the days you are going. There were some really good bands playing the day we went, but you needed to get tickets ahead of time. St. Paul's Chapel is right next door, built in 1700's and host to George Washington's Inaugeration, very historic and almost no damage from 9/11. If we would have known about that earlier we would have gone (we had only one day there). The rooms were very modern, the view overlooked all of Ground Zero. Bathrooms were large. Not many restaurants in the area so we ate at the hotel restaurant, Church and Dey. Very good. If you do want to go see Times Square or Central Park, the subway is right in front of the hotel. Very easy access. All in all, safe location, great hotel and lots of sights. Will stay there again when I go back to Lower Manhattan.
